## 1. Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus

Category: Diabetes and Blood Sugar Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module type_2_diabetes_mellitus_v1; validated intent matches: type_2_diabetes_mellitus_intent_v1 (288); type_1_diabetes_mellitus_intent_v1 (24)
Guidelines: ADA_SOC_2026; ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Measure current weight: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Weight change influences insulin resistance framing, nutrition plan, and medication selection. Rationale: Quantifies anthropometric and cardiometabolic risk so abnormal values can change diagnostic criteria, treatment selection, dosing context, or prevention intensity for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.

Clinical questions:
- How much are you drinking and urinating, including polyuria, polydipsia, overnight urination, thirst intensity, access to water, and any dehydration or confusion? Options: Fluid intake / Urine output / Polyuria / Polydipsia / Overnight urination / Thirst intensity / Access to water / Dehydration / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus needs urgent evaluation today. Management: A positive answer changes urgency from routine diabetes assessment to same-day hyperglycemia, ketosis, dehydration, infection, or insulin-delivery evaluation for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- How has weight changed from baseline, and was the change intentional or associated with appetite, fluid status, or systemic symptoms? - Any dysuria, urinary frequency or urgency, suprapubic pain, hematuria, or flank pain suggesting UTI or pyelonephritis? Options: No / Dysuria / Urinary frequency / Urgency / Suprapubic pain / Hematuria / Flank pain suggesting UTI / Pyelonephritis / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes the leading Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus pathway by refining severity, mimics, confirmatory testing, treatment safety, and follow-up timing. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Any foot ulcer, wound, skin redness, drainage, tenderness, indwelling line/device, or procedure-site concern suggesting infection? Options: No / Foot ulcer / Wound / Skin redness / Drainage / Tenderness / Indwelling line/device / Procedure-site concern suggesting infection / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus therapy unsafe. Management: Complication history changes risk staging, prevention priorities, medication selection, and follow-up intensity for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.

Options: No / History of ASCVD / Heart failure / Stroke/TIA / Peripheral arterial disease / Claudication / Vascular procedures / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus therapy unsafe. Management: The answer changes cardiometabolic risk stratification, prevention intensity, complication screening, and follow-up interval for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Inspect feet for ulcers: Inspect both feet including interdigital spaces and pressure points for ulcer, callus, erythema, drainage, deformity, or infection. Findings: No ulcer / Ulcer/wound / Callus/deformity / Infection concern / Unable to assess. Target: diabetic neuropathy, foot ulcer risk, infection, or peripheral arterial disease Management: An ulcer or wound changes infection workup, offloading, antibiotic planning, and disposition. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate pedal pulses: Palpate bilateral pulses at the named sites, comparing amplitude, symmetry, rhythm, and perfusion. Findings: Symmetric/normal / Diminished / Absent / Asymmetric / Unable to assess. Target: diabetic foot perfusion, peripheral arterial disease, or vascular risk Management: Diminished pulses change vascular risk assessment and foot-wound management. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Test monofilament sensation: Apply a 10-g monofilament perpendicular to standard plantar sites until it bends, with eyes closed, documenting sites felt or missed. Findings: Protective sensation intact / Reduced / Absent / Unable to assess. Target: diabetic neuropathy, foot ulcer risk, infection, or peripheral arterial disease Management: Loss of protective sensation changes foot-care counseling, footwear planning, and ulcer prevention. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment 10-g monofilament

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Observe Kussmaul breathing: Observe respiratory rate, depth, accessory muscle use, speech tolerance, and breathing pattern at rest. Findings: Absent / Deep/labored pattern / Respiratory distress / Unable to assess. Target: respiratory compensation, pulmonary congestion, infection, obstruction, or distress Management: Kussmaul breathing changes crisis severity and urgent treatment pathway. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate abdomen for tenderness: Inspect and palpate the abdomen gently, localizing tenderness and stopping if guarding, rebound, or severe pain occurs. Findings: Nontender / Tender / Guarding / Rebound/peritoneal concern / Unable to assess. Target: abdominal complication, endocrine crisis mimic, or precipitating illness Management: Tenderness changes precipitant evaluation and concern for surgical or pancreatitis mimic. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect insulin pump site: Inspect the infusion or device site for dislodgement, leakage, erythema, tenderness, occlusion, or supply failure. Findings: Site intact / Dislodged/occluded/leaking / Erythema/tenderness/drainage / Unable to assess. Target: insulin delivery failure, infusion-site infection, or device-related precipitant Management: Site failure changes precipitant assessment and insulin delivery plan. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect foot wound: Inspect both feet including interdigital spaces and pressure points for ulcer, callus, erythema, drainage, deformity, or infection. Findings: No ulcer / Ulcer/wound / Callus/deformity / Infection concern / Unable to assess. Target: diabetic neuropathy, foot ulcer risk, infection, or peripheral arterial disease Management: A wound changes infection workup, antibiotics, and disposition. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Diagnostic workup and reference values:
- A1c, fasting plasma glucose, or 2-hour OGTT to confirm.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: A1c: normal <5.7%; prediabetes 5.7-6.4%; diabetes >=6.5%. Fasting plasma glucose: normal <100 mg/dL; prediabetes 100-125; diabetes >=126. 2-hour 75-g OGTT: normal <140 mg/dL; prediabetes 140-199; diabetes >=200. Random plasma glucose >=200 mg/dL with classic symptoms supports diabetes diagnosis. UACR normal <30 mg/g; moderately increased 30-300; severely increased >300. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- A1c: normal <5.7%; prediabetes 5.7-6.4%; diabetes >=6.5%.
- Fasting plasma glucose: normal <100 mg/dL; prediabetes 100-125; diabetes >=126.
- 2-hour 75-g OGTT: normal <140 mg/dL; prediabetes 140-199; diabetes >=200.
- Random plasma glucose >=200 mg/dL with classic symptoms supports diabetes diagnosis.
- UACR normal <30 mg/g; moderately increased 30-300; severely increased >300.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- DKA/HHS symptoms, dehydration, vomiting, altered mental status.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Random glucose >=200 mg/dL with classic symptoms.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- DKA/HHS physiology, recurrent severe hypoglycemia, vomiting/dehydration, altered mental status, infected foot wound, or pregnancy with hyperglycemia.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.

Results that change management:
- Diabetes-range A1c/FPG/OGTT changes diagnosis and treatment intensity. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- UACR >=30 or reduced eGFR changes kidney-protective therapy. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026.
- Ketosis/acidosis, HHS osmolality, or severe hypoglycemia triggers urgent protocolized treatment rather than routine outpatient adjustment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- CKD, albuminuria, ASCVD/HF risk, pregnancy, foot infection, or insulin access barriers change medication choice and follow-up urgency. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Type 2 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026.

## 2. Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus

Category: Diabetes and Blood Sugar Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module type_1_diabetes_mellitus_v1; validated intent matches: type_1_diabetes_mellitus_intent_v1 (320); type_2_diabetes_mellitus_intent_v1 (24)
Guidelines: ADA_SOC_2026; ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026; ADA_HYPERGLYCEMIC_CRISES_2024

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Measure current weight: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Weight change influences insulin resistance framing, nutrition plan, and medication selection. Rationale: Quantifies anthropometric and cardiometabolic risk so abnormal values can change diagnostic criteria, treatment selection, dosing context, or prevention intensity for Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.

Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus needs urgent evaluation today. Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Inspect feet for ulcers: Inspect both feet including interdigital spaces and pressure points for ulcer, callus, erythema, drainage, deformity, or infection. Findings: No ulcer / Ulcer/wound / Callus/deformity / Infection concern / Unable to assess. Target: diabetic neuropathy, foot ulcer risk, infection, or peripheral arterial disease Management: An ulcer or wound changes infection workup, offloading, antibiotic planning, and disposition. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate pedal pulses: Palpate bilateral pulses at the named sites, comparing amplitude, symmetry, rhythm, and perfusion. Findings: Symmetric/normal / Diminished / Absent / Asymmetric / Unable to assess. Target: diabetic foot perfusion, peripheral arterial disease, or vascular risk Management: Diminished pulses change vascular risk assessment and foot-wound management. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Test monofilament sensation: Apply a 10-g monofilament perpendicular to standard plantar sites until it bends, with eyes closed, documenting sites felt or missed. Findings: Protective sensation intact / Reduced / Absent / Unable to assess. Target: diabetic neuropathy, foot ulcer risk, infection, or peripheral arterial disease Management: Loss of protective sensation changes foot-care counseling, footwear planning, and ulcer prevention. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment 10-g monofilament

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Observe Kussmaul breathing: Observe respiratory rate, depth, accessory muscle use, speech tolerance, and breathing pattern at rest. Findings: Absent / Deep/labored pattern / Respiratory distress / Unable to assess. Target: respiratory compensation, pulmonary congestion, infection, obstruction, or distress Management: Kussmaul breathing changes crisis severity and urgent treatment pathway. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate abdomen for tenderness: Inspect and palpate the abdomen gently, localizing tenderness and stopping if guarding, rebound, or severe pain occurs. Findings: Nontender / Tender / Guarding / Rebound/peritoneal concern / Unable to assess. Target: abdominal complication, endocrine crisis mimic, or precipitating illness Management: Tenderness changes precipitant evaluation and concern for surgical or pancreatitis mimic. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect insulin pump site: Inspect the infusion or device site for dislodgement, leakage, erythema, tenderness, occlusion, or supply failure. Findings: Site intact / Dislodged/occluded/leaking / Erythema/tenderness/drainage / Unable to assess. Target: insulin delivery failure, infusion-site infection, or device-related precipitant Management: Site failure changes precipitant assessment and insulin delivery plan. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect foot wound: Inspect both feet including interdigital spaces and pressure points for ulcer, callus, erythema, drainage, deformity, or infection. Findings: No ulcer / Ulcer/wound / Callus/deformity / Infection concern / Unable to assess. Target: diabetic neuropathy, foot ulcer risk, infection, or peripheral arterial disease Management: A wound changes infection workup, antibiotics, and disposition. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs. Source: ADA_SOC_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Fasting plasma glucose: normal <100 mg/dL; prediabetes 100-125; diabetes >=126. 2-hour 75-g OGTT: normal <140 mg/dL; prediabetes 140-199; diabetes >=200. Random plasma glucose >=200 mg/dL with classic symptoms supports diabetes diagnosis. DKA: diabetes/hyperglycemia plus ketosis plus metabolic acidosis; glucose may be lower in euglycemic DKA. DKA beta-hydroxybutyrate often >=3.0 mmol/L with pH <7.3 or bicarbonate <18 mmol/L. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. - A1c: normal <5.7%; prediabetes 5.7-6.4%; diabetes >=6.5%.

Red flags:
- Vomiting, dehydration, hypotension, Kussmaul respirations, altered mental status.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- SGLT2 inhibitor with ketotic symptoms even if glucose is not very high.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- DKA/HHS physiology, recurrent severe hypoglycemia, vomiting/dehydration, altered mental status, infected foot wound, or pregnancy with hyperglycemia.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.

- Ketosis plus acidosis requires urgent DKA pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Positive antibodies or low C-peptide supports autoimmune insulin-deficient diabetes. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_HYPERGLYCEMIC_CRISES_2024.

Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Ketosis/acidosis, HHS osmolality, or severe hypoglycemia triggers urgent protocolized treatment rather than routine outpatient adjustment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Type 1 Diabetes Mellitus. Source: ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026.

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- A1c: normal <5.7%; prediabetes 5.7-6.4%; diabetes >=6.5%.
- Fasting plasma glucose: normal <100 mg/dL; prediabetes 100-125; diabetes >=126.
- 2-hour 75-g OGTT: normal <140 mg/dL; prediabetes 140-199; diabetes >=200.
- Random plasma glucose >=200 mg/dL with classic symptoms supports diabetes diagnosis.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Diabetes-range glycemia or hyperglycemic symptoms.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Prediabetes presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Prediabetes presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Diabetes-range glycemia with classic symptoms, severe hypertension, ASCVD symptoms, pregnancy-context hyperglycemia, or dehydration requires escalation beyond routine prevention care.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Prediabetes presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.

Results that change management:
- A1c 5.7-6.4, FPG 100-125, or 2-hour OGTT 140-199 triggers prevention and surveillance. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Prediabetes. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Diabetes-range values change diagnosis. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Prediabetes. Source: ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026.
- Markedly abnormal glucose, severe hypertension, pregnancy-context concern, or cardiopulmonary symptoms changes disposition from prevention visit to urgent evaluation. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Prediabetes. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Prediabetes. Source: ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026.
- Prediabetes or metabolic syndrome thresholds change prevention intensity, lifestyle intervention, cardiometabolic risk-factor treatment, and surveillance interval. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Prediabetes. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Diabetes-range glycemia, ASCVD/HF/CKD risk, fatty liver, obstructive sleep apnea, PCOS, or pregnancy context changes diagnostic classification, treatment safety, and referral or follow-up urgency. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Prediabetes. Source: ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026.

## 4. Gestational Diabetes

Category: Diabetes and Blood Sugar Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module gestational_diabetes_v1; validated intent matches: gestational_diabetes_intent_v1 (284)
Guidelines: ADA_SOC_2026; ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Gestational Diabetes. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Gestational Diabetes. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Measure current weight: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Weight change influences insulin resistance framing, nutrition plan, and medication selection. Rationale: Quantifies anthropometric and cardiometabolic risk so abnormal values can change diagnostic criteria, treatment selection, dosing context, or prevention intensity for Gestational Diabetes. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Measure waist circumference: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Central adiposity changes metabolic syndrome criteria and cardiometabolic risk framing. Rationale: Quantifies anthropometric and cardiometabolic risk so abnormal values can change diagnostic criteria, treatment selection, dosing context, or prevention intensity for Gestational Diabetes. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.

Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Gestational Diabetes. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- One-step 75-g OGTT for GDM: fasting >=92, 1-hour >=180, or 2-hour >=153 mg/dL.
- Two-step approach if used: 50-g screen often >=130-140 mg/dL; 100-g Carpenter-Coustan thresholds fasting 95, 1-hour 180, 2-hour 155, 3-hour 140 mg/dL, usually 2 abnormal values.
- A1c: normal <5.7%; prediabetes 5.7-6.4%; diabetes >=6.5%.
- Fasting plasma glucose: normal <100 mg/dL; prediabetes 100-125; diabetes >=126.
- 2-hour 75-g OGTT: normal <140 mg/dL; prediabetes 140-199; diabetes >=200.
- Random plasma glucose >=200 mg/dL with classic symptoms supports diabetes diagnosis.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Ketones, vomiting/dehydration, severe hyperglycemia.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Gestational Diabetes presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Hypertension or preeclampsia features.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Gestational Diabetes presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Gestational Diabetes presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Ketones, vomiting/dehydration, severe hyperglycemia, altered mental status, hypertension/preeclampsia features, or reduced fetal movement requires urgent obstetric/endocrine evaluation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Gestational Diabetes presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.

Results that change management:
- OGTT threshold crossing changes maternal/fetal monitoring and therapy. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Gestational Diabetes. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Postpartum abnormal OGTT changes long-term prevention. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Gestational Diabetes. Source: ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Gestational Diabetes. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Gestational Diabetes. Source: ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026.
- OGTT threshold crossing changes maternal-fetal monitoring, nutrition therapy, glucose monitoring, medication escalation, and delivery/postpartum planning. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Gestational Diabetes. Source: ADA_SOC_2026.
- Ketones, vomiting/dehydration, severe hyperglycemia, altered mental status, or hypertensive features in pregnancy changes disposition to urgent obstetric/endocrine evaluation. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Gestational Diabetes. Source: ADA_DIAGNOSIS_2026.

Diagnostic workup and reference values:

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context.
- Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay.
- T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Myxedema coma features: hypothermia, bradycardia, hypotension, hypoventilation, hyponatremia, altered mental status.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypothyroidism (Underactive Thyroid) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypothyroidism (Underactive Thyroid) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- Thyroid storm, myxedema coma, atrial fibrillation/heart failure, vision-threatening orbitopathy, rapidly enlarging neck mass, hoarseness, dysphagia, dyspnea, or suspicious nodes.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypothyroidism (Underactive Thyroid) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.

Results that change management:
- High TSH plus low FT4 confirms overt primary hypothyroidism. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypothyroidism (Underactive Thyroid). Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- Low FT4 with low/normal TSH triggers central hypothyroidism/pituitary pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypothyroidism (Underactive Thyroid). Source: AACE_ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2012.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypothyroidism (Underactive Thyroid). Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypothyroidism (Underactive Thyroid). Source: AACE_ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2012.
- Suppressed TSH with elevated T4/T3 changes to thyrotoxicosis severity and etiology workup; low FT4 with low/normal TSH triggers central hypothyroidism evaluation. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypothyroidism (Underactive Thyroid). Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- Suspicious nodule, compressive symptom, abnormal node, calcitonin/RET concern, or high-risk ultrasound feature changes imaging/FNA/surgical referral pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypothyroidism (Underactive Thyroid). Source: AACE_ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2012.

## 7. Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism)

Category: Thyroid Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module hashimotos_thyroiditis_v1; validated intent matches: hashimotos_thyroiditis_intent_v1 (345); routine_thyroid_disease_v1 (96); hypothyroidism_intent_v1 (81)
Guidelines: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014; AACE_ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2012; ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015; ETA_THYROID_NODULE_2023

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.

Clinical questions:
- Have you had cold intolerance, constipation, fatigue, dry skin, slowed thinking, hoarse voice, weight gain, or heavy menses? Options: Cold intolerance / Constipation / Fatigue / Dry skin / Slowed thinking / Hoarse voice / Weight gain / Heavy menses / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism) needs urgent evaluation today. Management: A positive answer raises concern for thyroid hormone deficiency or myxedema physiology and changes TSH/free T4 interpretation, replacement planning, and emergency-risk screening for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- Any personal or family autoimmune disease, endocrine disease, thyroid cancer/MEN2, adrenal disease, or related inherited condition? Options: No / Personal / Family autoimmune disease / Endocrine disease / Thyroid cancer/MEN2 / Adrenal disease / Related inherited condition / Other ___. Purpose: Defines the patient-specific context needed to interpret endocrine tests, avoid common mimics, and choose the safest next step for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Management: The answer changes thyroid ultrasound/FNA urgency, compressive-symptom escalation, cancer-risk framing, and endocrine or surgical referral timing for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.

Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism) needs urgent evaluation today. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- Any palpitations, tremor, heat intolerance, anxiety, insomnia, weight loss, diarrhea, or sweating suggesting thyroid hormone excess or adrenergic physiology? Options: No / Palpitations / Tremor / Heat intolerance / Anxiety / Insomnia / Weight loss / Diarrhea / Sweating suggesting thyroid hormone excess / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism) needs urgent evaluation today. Management: A positive answer raises concern for thyroid hormone excess or thyroid storm and changes beta-blocker need, thyroid testing urgency, trigger search, and emergency endocrine escalation for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- How has weight changed from baseline, and was the change intentional or associated with appetite, fluid status, or systemic symptoms? Options: Weight change from baseline / Intentional weight change / Appetite change / Fluid-status change / Systemic symptoms / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism) needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes cardiometabolic risk stratification, prevention intensity, complication screening, and follow-up interval for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- When was the last menstrual period, how regular are cycles, and has bleeding changed from baseline? Options: Not possible / Possible / Known pregnant/postpartum / Timing/dating known / Unknown / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism) needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes the leading Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism) pathway by refining severity, mimics, confirmatory testing, treatment safety, and follow-up timing. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- Any neck swelling, thyroid pain or tenderness, pressure, hoarseness, trouble swallowing, positional shortness of breath, or rapidly enlarging neck mass? Options: No / Neck swelling / Thyroid pain / Tenderness / Pressure / Hoarseness / Trouble swallowing / Positional shortness of breath / Rapidly enlarging neck mass / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism) needs urgent evaluation today. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.

Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.

Conditional history add-ons:
- None.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Palpate thyroid gland: Inspect and palpate the thyroid from in front or behind while the patient swallows, noting size, tenderness, asymmetry, nodules, fixation, or bruit if auscultated. Findings: Normal size / Goiter / Nodule/asymmetry / Tender / Fixed/hard / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid structural disease, compressive features, or thyroid inflammatory/autoimmune pattern Management: Goiter, tenderness, asymmetry, or a dominant nodule changes etiology and imaging decisions. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate cervical lymph nodes: Palpate cervical and supraclavicular nodal chains systematically, noting size, tenderness, mobility, firmness, and laterality. Findings: No concerning nodes / Tender/mobile nodes / Firm/fixed nodes / Supraclavicular node / Unable to assess. Target: regional nodal disease or thyroid malignancy risk Management: Suspicious lymph nodes change ultrasound mapping, biopsy planning, and urgency. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Auscultate heart rhythm: Auscultate the precordium with diaphragm and bell as appropriate, noting rate regularity, extra sounds, murmurs, rubs, or gallop. Findings: Regular / Irregular / Tachycardic / Bradycardic / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid-related tachycardia, atrial fibrillation, bradycardia, or heart-failure complication Management: Irregular rhythm changes ECG need, beta-blocker consideration, and escalation. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment stethoscope
- Observe outstretched-hands tremor: Ask the patient to extend both arms and spread fingers; observe for fine tremor and functional impact. Findings: No tremor / Fine tremor / Coarse tremor / Functionally limiting tremor / Unable to assess. Target: thyrotoxicosis adrenergic signs, medication effect, or endocrine-related neuromuscular irritability Management: Fine tremor supports adrenergic thyrotoxicosis and changes symptom-control decisions. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Listen to voice quality: Listen to voice quality during normal speech and ask about new hoarseness, weak voice, or compressive symptoms. Findings: Normal voice / Hoarse / Weak/breathy / Stridor/airway concern / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid structural disease, compressive features, or thyroid inflammatory/autoimmune pattern Management: Hoarseness changes concern for recurrent laryngeal nerve involvement and surgical urgency. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect neck for airway narrowing: Inspect neck contour and observe breathing/stridor; ask about positional dyspnea while avoiding provocative maneuvers in unstable patients. Findings: No visible narrowing / Large goiter/mass effect / Stridor/positional dyspnea / Unable to assess. Target: encephalopathy, crisis severity, or airway-protection risk Management: Airway concern changes urgency and imaging or procedural planning. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Inspect eyelid retraction: Inspect eyes and eyelids from the front and side for lid lag/retraction, proptosis, conjunctival injection, or exposure signs. Findings: Absent / Present / Asymmetric / Exposure concern / Unable to assess. Target: thyrotoxicosis adrenergic signs or Graves orbitopathy severity Management: Lid retraction supports Graves or adrenergic thyroid physiology and changes etiology assessment. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Test extraocular movements: Ask the patient to follow a target through cardinal gaze positions and observe for limitation, pain, diplopia, or nystagmus. Findings: Full / Restricted / Diplopia / Painful / Unable to assess. Target: Graves orbitopathy, diplopia, ocular motility restriction, or vision-threatening thyroid eye disease Management: Restriction changes orbitopathy severity and eye-care urgency. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

- Thyroid storm, myxedema coma, atrial fibrillation/heart failure, vision-threatening orbitopathy, rapidly enlarging neck mass, hoarseness, dysphagia, dyspnea, or suspicious nodes.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.

Results that change management:
- Positive TPO Ab supports autoimmune thyroiditis. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- Suspicious nodule/compressive findings move to ultrasound/FNA pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: AACE_ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2012.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: ETA_THYROID_NODULE_2023.
- Suppressed TSH with elevated T4/T3 changes to thyrotoxicosis severity and etiology workup; low FT4 with low/normal TSH triggers central hypothyroidism evaluation. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2014.
- Suspicious nodule, compressive symptom, abnormal node, calcitonin/RET concern, or high-risk ultrasound feature changes imaging/FNA/surgical referral pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hashimoto's Thyroiditis (Autoimmune Hypothyroidism). Source: AACE_ATA_HYPOTHYROIDISM_2012.

Conditional history add-ons:
- None.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Palpate thyroid gland: Inspect and palpate the thyroid from in front or behind while the patient swallows, noting size, tenderness, asymmetry, nodules, fixation, or bruit if auscultated. Findings: Normal size / Goiter / Nodule/asymmetry / Tender / Fixed/hard / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid structural disease, compressive features, or thyroid inflammatory/autoimmune pattern Management: Goiter, tenderness, asymmetry, or a dominant nodule changes etiology and imaging decisions. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate cervical lymph nodes: Palpate cervical and supraclavicular nodal chains systematically, noting size, tenderness, mobility, firmness, and laterality. Findings: No concerning nodes / Tender/mobile nodes / Firm/fixed nodes / Supraclavicular node / Unable to assess. Target: regional nodal disease or thyroid malignancy risk Management: Suspicious lymph nodes change ultrasound mapping, biopsy planning, and urgency. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Auscultate heart rhythm: Auscultate the precordium with diaphragm and bell as appropriate, noting rate regularity, extra sounds, murmurs, rubs, or gallop. Findings: Regular / Irregular / Tachycardic / Bradycardic / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid-related tachycardia, atrial fibrillation, bradycardia, or heart-failure complication Management: Irregular rhythm changes ECG need, beta-blocker consideration, and escalation. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment stethoscope
- Observe outstretched-hands tremor: Ask the patient to extend both arms and spread fingers; observe for fine tremor and functional impact. Findings: No tremor / Fine tremor / Coarse tremor / Functionally limiting tremor / Unable to assess. Target: thyrotoxicosis adrenergic signs, medication effect, or endocrine-related neuromuscular irritability Management: Fine tremor supports adrenergic thyrotoxicosis and changes symptom-control decisions. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect eyes for proptosis: Inspect eyes and eyelids from the front and side for lid lag/retraction, proptosis, conjunctival injection, or exposure signs. Findings: Absent / Mild / Marked / Vision/exposure concern / Unable to assess. Target: thyrotoxicosis adrenergic signs or Graves orbitopathy severity Management: Proptosis changes orbitopathy severity assessment and ophthalmology urgency. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Test extraocular movements: Ask the patient to follow a target through cardinal gaze positions and observe for limitation, pain, diplopia, or nystagmus. Findings: Full / Restricted / Diplopia / Painful / Unable to assess. Target: Graves orbitopathy, diplopia, ocular motility restriction, or vision-threatening thyroid eye disease Management: Restricted movement changes orbitopathy severity and urgent eye-care needs. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Target: regional nodal disease or thyroid malignancy risk Management: Suspicious lymph nodes change ultrasound mapping, biopsy planning, and urgency. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Auscultate heart rhythm: Auscultate the precordium with diaphragm and bell as appropriate, noting rate regularity, extra sounds, murmurs, rubs, or gallop. Findings: Regular / Irregular / Tachycardic / Bradycardic / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid-related tachycardia, atrial fibrillation, bradycardia, or heart-failure complication Management: Irregular rhythm changes ECG need, beta-blocker consideration, and escalation. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment stethoscope
- Observe outstretched-hands tremor: Ask the patient to extend both arms and spread fingers; observe for fine tremor and functional impact. Findings: No tremor / Fine tremor / Coarse tremor / Functionally limiting tremor / Unable to assess. Target: thyrotoxicosis adrenergic signs, medication effect, or endocrine-related neuromuscular irritability Management: Fine tremor supports adrenergic thyrotoxicosis and changes symptom-control decisions. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect eyes for proptosis: Inspect eyes and eyelids from the front and side for lid lag/retraction, proptosis, conjunctival injection, or exposure signs. Findings: Absent / Mild / Marked / Vision/exposure concern / Unable to assess. Target: thyrotoxicosis adrenergic signs or Graves orbitopathy severity Management: Proptosis changes orbitopathy severity assessment and ophthalmology urgency. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Test extraocular movements: Ask the patient to follow a target through cardinal gaze positions and observe for limitation, pain, diplopia, or nystagmus. Findings: Full / Restricted / Diplopia / Painful / Unable to assess. Target: Graves orbitopathy, diplopia, ocular motility restriction, or vision-threatening thyroid eye disease Management: Restricted movement changes orbitopathy severity and urgent eye-care needs. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Inspect eyelid retraction: Inspect eyes and eyelids from the front and side for lid lag/retraction, proptosis, conjunctival injection, or exposure signs. Findings: Absent / Present / Asymmetric / Exposure concern / Unable to assess. Target: thyrotoxicosis adrenergic signs or Graves orbitopathy severity Management: Lid retraction supports Graves or adrenergic thyroid physiology and changes etiology assessment. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Listen to voice quality: Listen to voice quality during normal speech and ask about new hoarseness, weak voice, or compressive symptoms. Findings: Normal voice / Hoarse / Weak/breathy / Stridor/airway concern / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid structural disease, compressive features, or thyroid inflammatory/autoimmune pattern Management: Hoarseness changes airway and malignancy concern. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Diagnostic workup and reference values:
- TSH, free T4, T3.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context. Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay. T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- TRAb/TSI.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context. Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay. T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Confirms the diagnosis, identifies mimics or complications, or establishes a baseline that changes treatment for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- RAIU if TRAb negative, nodular, or unclear.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context. Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay. T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Confirms the diagnosis, identifies mimics or complications, or establishes a baseline that changes treatment for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Compare with prior results and repeat discordant nonurgent endocrine tests using correct timing, local assay, and interference precautions.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context. Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay. T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Confirms the diagnosis, identifies mimics or complications, or establishes a baseline that changes treatment for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Thyrotoxicosis safety data: check TSH, free T4, total T3, TRAb/TSI or RAIU as indicated, ECG for tachyarrhythmia, CBC/liver baseline before antithyroid drugs, and pregnancy testing before radioiodine or teratogenic treatment decisions.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context. Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay. T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- TSH with free T4; add T3 for thyrotoxicosis, TPO Ab for autoimmune hypothyroidism, TRAb/TSI for Graves, and thyroid ultrasound/FNA pathway for nodules.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context. Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay. T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Hold high-dose biotin before susceptible assays when feasible and interpret thyroid labs with pregnancy, acute illness, and central hypothyroidism context.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context. Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay. T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Confirms the diagnosis, identifies mimics or complications, or establishes a baseline that changes treatment for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context.: Use as a diagnostic anchor; confirm with local laboratory assay, pregnancy/age/sex context, and acute illness context. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay.: Use as a diagnostic anchor; confirm with local laboratory assay, pregnancy/age/sex context, and acute illness context. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific.: Use as a diagnostic anchor; confirm with local laboratory assay, pregnancy/age/sex context, and acute illness context. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.: Use as a diagnostic anchor; confirm with local laboratory assay, pregnancy/age/sex context, and acute illness context. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context.
- Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay.
- T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Thyroid storm, vision-threatening orbitopathy, pregnancy with uncontrolled hyperthyroidism.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Graves' Disease presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Graves' Disease presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Thyroid storm, myxedema coma, atrial fibrillation/heart failure, vision-threatening orbitopathy, rapidly enlarging neck mass, hoarseness, dysphagia, dyspnea, or suspicious nodes.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Graves' Disease presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.

Results that change management:
- TRAb-positive biochemical hyperthyroidism supports Graves. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Orbitopathy changes radioactive iodine risk and ophthalmology urgency. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Suppressed TSH with elevated T4/T3 changes to thyrotoxicosis severity and etiology workup; low FT4 with low/normal TSH triggers central hypothyroidism evaluation. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Suspicious nodule, compressive symptom, abnormal node, calcitonin/RET concern, or high-risk ultrasound feature changes imaging/FNA/surgical referral pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Graves' Disease. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.

## 10. Thyrotoxicosis

Category: Thyroid Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module thyrotoxicosis_v1; validated intent matches: thyrotoxicosis_intent_v1 (279); routine_thyroid_disease_v1 (123)
Guidelines: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.

Clinical questions:
- Do you have anterior neck pain or thyroid tenderness, painful swallowing, recent viral illness, fever, or postpartum timing suggesting thyroiditis? Options: Not possible / Possible / Known pregnant/postpartum / Timing/dating known / Unknown / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Thyrotoxicosis therapy unsafe. Management: A positive answer raises concern for thyroid hormone excess or thyroid storm and changes beta-blocker need, thyroid testing urgency, trigger search, and emergency endocrine escalation for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Any thyroid hormone, antithyroid drug, amiodarone, lithium, iodine/contrast exposure, biotin, supplement use, missed dose, or recent dose change affecting thyroid interpretation? Options: No relevant exposure / Medication change / Supplement use / Missed doses / Biotin / Iodine/contrast exposure / Hormone therapy / Recent treatment change / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Thyrotoxicosis therapy unsafe. Management: Positive exposure changes whether to hold interfering agents, repeat testing, adjust treatment, or use a safer Thyrotoxicosis pathway. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Any palpitations, tremor, heat intolerance, anxiety, insomnia, weight loss, diarrhea, or sweating suggesting thyroid hormone excess or adrenergic physiology? Options: No / Palpitations / Tremor / Heat intolerance / Anxiety / Insomnia / Weight loss / Diarrhea / Sweating suggesting thyroid hormone excess / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Thyrotoxicosis needs urgent evaluation today. Management: A positive answer raises concern for thyroid hormone excess or thyroid storm and changes beta-blocker need, thyroid testing urgency, trigger search, and emergency endocrine escalation for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- How has weight changed from baseline, and was the change intentional or associated with appetite, fluid status, or systemic symptoms? Options: Weight change from baseline / Intentional weight change / Appetite change / Fluid-status change / Systemic symptoms / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Thyrotoxicosis needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes cardiometabolic risk stratification, prevention intensity, complication screening, and follow-up interval for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Any fatigue, cold intolerance, constipation, dry skin, hoarse voice, slowed thinking, depression, heavy menses, or weight gain suggesting hypothyroidism? Options: No / Fatigue / Cold intolerance / Constipation / Dry skin / Hoarse voice / Slowed thinking / Depression / Heavy menses / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Thyrotoxicosis needs urgent evaluation today. Management: A positive answer raises concern for thyroid hormone deficiency or myxedema physiology and changes TSH/free T4 interpretation, replacement planning, and emergency-risk screening for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Any anxiety, depression, irritability, slowed thinking, memory change, confusion, sleep change, or functional decline? Options: No / Anxiety / Depression / Irritability / Slowed thinking / Memory change / Confusion / Sleep change / Functional decline / Other ___. Purpose: Defines the patient-specific context needed to interpret endocrine tests, avoid common mimics, and choose the safest next step for Thyrotoxicosis. Management: A positive answer raises concern for thyroid hormone deficiency or myxedema physiology and changes TSH/free T4 interpretation, replacement planning, and emergency-risk screening for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- When was the last menstrual period, how regular are cycles, and has bleeding changed from baseline? Options: Not possible / Possible / Known pregnant/postpartum / Timing/dating known / Unknown / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Thyrotoxicosis needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes the leading Thyrotoxicosis pathway by refining severity, mimics, confirmatory testing, treatment safety, and follow-up timing. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Any neck swelling, thyroid pain or tenderness, pressure, hoarseness, trouble swallowing, positional shortness of breath, or rapidly enlarging neck mass? Options: No / Neck swelling / Thyroid pain / Tenderness / Pressure / Hoarseness / Trouble swallowing / Positional shortness of breath / Rapidly enlarging neck mass / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Thyrotoxicosis needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes thyroid ultrasound/FNA urgency, compressive-symptom escalation, cancer-risk framing, and endocrine or surgical referral timing for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Any childhood head/neck radiation, therapeutic radiation, occupational exposure, or family thyroid cancer risk factor? Options: No / Childhood head/neck radiation / Therapeutic radiation / Occupational exposure / Family thyroid cancer risk factor / Other ___. Purpose: Defines the patient-specific context needed to interpret endocrine tests, avoid common mimics, and choose the safest next step for Thyrotoxicosis. Management: The answer changes thyroid ultrasound/FNA urgency, compressive-symptom escalation, cancer-risk framing, and endocrine or surgical referral timing for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Any personal or family history of MEN, VHL, NF1, SDHx-related tumors, medullary thyroid cancer, pheochromocytoma, paraganglioma, or adrenal/pituitary tumors? Options: No / Personal / Family history of MEN / VHL / NF1 / SDHx-related tumors / Medullary thyroid cancer / Pheochromocytoma / Paraganglioma / Other ___. Purpose: Defines the patient-specific context needed to interpret endocrine tests, avoid common mimics, and choose the safest next step for Thyrotoxicosis. Management: The answer changes central endocrine localization, pituitary MRI or visual-field review, axis testing, and neurosurgical or ophthalmology escalation for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.

Conditional history add-ons:
- None.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Palpate thyroid gland: Inspect and palpate the thyroid from in front or behind while the patient swallows, noting size, tenderness, asymmetry, nodules, fixation, or bruit if auscultated. Findings: Normal size / Goiter / Nodule/asymmetry / Tender / Fixed/hard / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid structural disease, compressive features, or thyroid inflammatory/autoimmune pattern Management: Goiter, tenderness, asymmetry, or a dominant nodule changes etiology and imaging decisions. Rationale: Confirms the diagnosis, identifies mimics or complications, or establishes a baseline that changes treatment for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context.: Use as a diagnostic anchor; confirm with local laboratory assay, pregnancy/age/sex context, and acute illness context. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay.: Use as a diagnostic anchor; confirm with local laboratory assay, pregnancy/age/sex context, and acute illness context. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.

Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.: Use as a diagnostic anchor; confirm with local laboratory assay, pregnancy/age/sex context, and acute illness context. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context.
- Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay.
- T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Storm physiology, AF, heart failure, severe weight loss, altered mental status.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Thyrotoxicosis presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Thyrotoxicosis presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Thyroid storm, myxedema coma, atrial fibrillation/heart failure, vision-threatening orbitopathy, rapidly enlarging neck mass, hoarseness, dysphagia, dyspnea, or suspicious nodes.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Thyrotoxicosis presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.

Results that change management:
- Low uptake changes management away from antithyroid drugs toward thyroiditis/supportive pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Suppressed TSH with elevated T4/T3 changes to thyrotoxicosis severity and etiology workup; low FT4 with low/normal TSH triggers central hypothyroidism evaluation. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.
- Suspicious nodule, compressive symptom, abnormal node, calcitonin/RET concern, or high-risk ultrasound feature changes imaging/FNA/surgical referral pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Thyrotoxicosis. Source: ATA_HYPERTHYROIDISM_2016.

## 11. Thyroid Nodules (Benign)

Category: Thyroid Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module thyroid_nodules_v1; validated intent matches: thyroid_nodules_intent_v1 (350); routine_thyroid_disease_v1 (87)
Guidelines: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015; ETA_THYROID_NODULE_2023

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Thyroid Nodules (Benign). Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Thyroid Nodules (Benign). Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015.

Management: A positive answer raises concern for thyroid hormone excess or thyroid storm and changes beta-blocker need, thyroid testing urgency, trigger search, and emergency endocrine escalation for Thyroid Nodules (Benign).
