Conditional history add-ons:
- None.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Palpate thyroid gland: Inspect and palpate the thyroid from in front or behind while the patient swallows, noting size, tenderness, asymmetry, nodules, fixation, or bruit if auscultated. Findings: Normal size / Goiter / Nodule/asymmetry / Tender / Fixed/hard / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid structural disease, compressive features, or thyroid inflammatory/autoimmune pattern Management: Goiter, tenderness, asymmetry, or a dominant nodule changes etiology and imaging decisions. Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate cervical lymph nodes: Palpate cervical and supraclavicular nodal chains systematically, noting size, tenderness, mobility, firmness, and laterality. Findings: No concerning nodes / Tender/mobile nodes / Firm/fixed nodes / Supraclavicular node / Unable to assess. Target: regional nodal disease or thyroid malignancy risk Management: Suspicious lymph nodes change ultrasound mapping, biopsy planning, and urgency. Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Auscultate heart rhythm: Auscultate the precordium with diaphragm and bell as appropriate, noting rate regularity, extra sounds, murmurs, rubs, or gallop. Findings: Regular / Irregular / Tachycardic / Bradycardic / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid-related tachycardia, atrial fibrillation, bradycardia, or heart-failure complication Management: Irregular rhythm changes ECG need, beta-blocker consideration, and escalation. Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment stethoscope
- Observe outstretched-hands tremor: Ask the patient to extend both arms and spread fingers; observe for fine tremor and functional impact. Findings: No tremor / Fine tremor / Coarse tremor / Functionally limiting tremor / Unable to assess. Target: thyrotoxicosis adrenergic signs, medication effect, or endocrine-related neuromuscular irritability Management: Fine tremor supports adrenergic thyrotoxicosis and changes symptom-control decisions. Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Listen to voice quality: Listen to voice quality during normal speech and ask about new hoarseness, weak voice, or compressive symptoms. Findings: Normal voice / Hoarse / Weak/breathy / Stridor/airway concern / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid structural disease, compressive features, or thyroid inflammatory/autoimmune pattern Management: Hoarseness changes concern for recurrent laryngeal nerve involvement and surgical urgency. Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect neck for airway narrowing: Inspect neck contour and observe breathing/stridor; ask about positional dyspnea while avoiding provocative maneuvers in unstable patients. Findings: No visible narrowing / Large goiter/mass effect / Stridor/positional dyspnea / Unable to assess. Target: encephalopathy, crisis severity, or airway-protection risk Management: Airway concern changes urgency and imaging or procedural planning. Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Inspect eyelid retraction: Inspect eyes and eyelids from the front and side for lid lag/retraction, proptosis, conjunctival injection, or exposure signs. Findings: Absent / Present / Asymmetric / Exposure concern / Unable to assess. Target: thyrotoxicosis adrenergic signs or Graves orbitopathy severity Management: Lid retraction supports Graves or adrenergic thyroid physiology and changes etiology assessment. Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Test extraocular movements: Ask the patient to follow a target through cardinal gaze positions and observe for limitation, pain, diplopia, or nystagmus. Findings: Full / Restricted / Diplopia / Painful / Unable to assess. Target: Graves orbitopathy, diplopia, ocular motility restriction, or vision-threatening thyroid eye disease Management: Restriction changes orbitopathy severity and eye-care urgency. Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs. Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Palpate thyroid gland: Inspect and palpate the thyroid from in front or behind while the patient swallows, noting size, tenderness, asymmetry, nodules, fixation, or bruit if auscultated. Findings: Normal size / Goiter / Nodule/asymmetry / Tender / Fixed/hard / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid structural disease, compressive features, or thyroid inflammatory/autoimmune pattern Management: Goiter, tenderness, asymmetry, or a dominant nodule changes etiology and imaging decisions. Source: ATA_THYROID_CANCER_2025; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate cervical lymph nodes: Palpate cervical and supraclavicular nodal chains systematically, noting size, tenderness, mobility, firmness, and laterality. Findings: No concerning nodes / Tender/mobile nodes / Firm/fixed nodes / Supraclavicular node / Unable to assess. Target: regional nodal disease or thyroid malignancy risk Management: Suspicious lymph nodes change ultrasound mapping, biopsy planning, and urgency. Source: ATA_THYROID_CANCER_2025; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Auscultate heart rhythm: Auscultate the precordium with diaphragm and bell as appropriate, noting rate regularity, extra sounds, murmurs, rubs, or gallop. Findings: Regular / Irregular / Tachycardic / Bradycardic / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid-related tachycardia, atrial fibrillation, bradycardia, or heart-failure complication Management: Irregular rhythm changes ECG need, beta-blocker consideration, and escalation. Source: ATA_THYROID_CANCER_2025; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment stethoscope
- Observe outstretched-hands tremor: Ask the patient to extend both arms and spread fingers; observe for fine tremor and functional impact. Findings: No tremor / Fine tremor / Coarse tremor / Functionally limiting tremor / Unable to assess. Target: thyrotoxicosis adrenergic signs, medication effect, or endocrine-related neuromuscular irritability Management: Fine tremor supports adrenergic thyrotoxicosis and changes symptom-control decisions. Source: ATA_THYROID_CANCER_2025; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Listen to voice quality: Listen to voice quality during normal speech and ask about new hoarseness, weak voice, or compressive symptoms. Findings: Normal voice / Hoarse / Weak/breathy / Stridor/airway concern / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid structural disease, compressive features, or thyroid inflammatory/autoimmune pattern Management: Hoarseness changes concern for recurrent laryngeal nerve involvement and surgical urgency. Findings: No visible narrowing / Large goiter/mass effect / Stridor/positional dyspnea / Unable to assess. Target: encephalopathy, crisis severity, or airway-protection risk Management: Airway concern changes urgency and imaging or procedural planning. Source: ATA_THYROID_CANCER_2025; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Results that change management:
- Bethesda V/VI, suspicious nodes, calcitonin/CEA elevation, or RET positivity changes surgical/genetic pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Thyroid Cancer (Papillary, Follicular, Medullary). Source: ATA_THYROID_CANCER_2025.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Thyroid Cancer (Papillary, Follicular, Medullary). Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Thyroid Cancer (Papillary, Follicular, Medullary). Source: ETA_THYROID_NODULE_2023.
- Suppressed TSH with elevated T4/T3 changes to thyrotoxicosis severity and etiology workup; low FT4 with low/normal TSH triggers central hypothyroidism evaluation. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Thyroid Cancer (Papillary, Follicular, Medullary). Source: ATA_THYROID_CANCER_2025.
- Suspicious nodule, compressive symptom, abnormal node, calcitonin/RET concern, or high-risk ultrasound feature changes imaging/FNA/surgical referral pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Thyroid Cancer (Papillary, Follicular, Medullary). Source: ATA_THYROID_NODULE_DTC_2015.

## 13. Osteoporosis

Category: Bone and Parathyroid Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module osteoporosis_v1; validated intent matches: osteoporosis_intent_v1 (279)
Guidelines: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; AACE_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Osteoporosis. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Osteoporosis. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.

Clinical questions:
- Any height loss, new back pain, kyphosis, low-trauma fracture, fall, neurologic symptom, or steroid exposure suggesting vertebral compression or bone fragility? Options: No / Height loss / New back pain / Kyphosis / Low-trauma fracture / Fall / Neurologic symptom / Steroid exposure suggesting vertebral compression / Bone fragility / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Osteoporosis therapy unsafe. Management: The answer changes fracture risk, calcium/vitamin D/PTH interpretation, imaging threshold, replacement urgency, and fall-prevention planning for Osteoporosis. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Test proximal hip flexor strength: Test hip flexion strength against resistance bilaterally while the patient is seated or supine, adapting to pain and safety. Findings: Normal strength / Mild weakness / Needs arms/assistance / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Weakness changes fall risk, severity assessment, and urgency of calcium or vitamin D evaluation. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate focal bone tenderness: Palpate the symptomatic bone or spine area gently for focal tenderness and correlate with trauma, fracture risk, and neurologic symptoms. Findings: No focal tenderness / Focal tenderness / Diffuse tenderness / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Focal tenderness changes fracture concern, imaging need, and treatment urgency. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Observe gait stability if safe: Observe standing and gait only if safe, noting balance, antalgia, assistive-device need, and fall risk. Findings: Stable / Unsteady / Needs assistive device/help / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Unsafe gait changes fall precautions, disposition, and rehabilitation planning. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect spine posture for kyphosis: Inspect standing posture and spinal curvature, noting kyphosis, height-loss concern, or vertebral compression pattern. Findings: No kyphosis/height-loss concern / Kyphosis / Height-loss concern / Unable to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Kyphosis or height-loss concern changes vertebral fracture evaluation and imaging threshold. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Palpate spine for focal tenderness: Palpate the symptomatic bone or spine area gently for focal tenderness and correlate with trauma, fracture risk, and neurologic symptoms. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Focal tenderness changes fracture imaging threshold. - Elicit Chvostek sign: Tap over the facial nerve anterior to the ear and observe for ipsilateral facial twitching, interpreting cautiously because false positives occur. Findings: Negative / Positive / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Positive Chvostek sign changes urgency of calcium testing and replacement. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Elicit Trousseau sign: Inflate a blood-pressure cuff above systolic pressure for up to three minutes if safe and observe for carpopedal spasm. Findings: Negative / Positive / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Positive Trousseau sign changes urgency of calcium replacement and monitoring. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment blood pressure cuff
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Diagnostic workup and reference values:
- DXA and vertebral imaging when indicated.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: Corrected calcium often about 8.5-10.5 mg/dL; ionized calcium about 1.12-1.32 mmol/L; use local lab. Intact PTH often about 10-65 pg/mL but assay-specific. DXA T-score: normal >= -1.0; osteopenia -1.0 to -2.5; osteoporosis <= -2.5. 25(OH)D thresholds vary; many labs flag <20 ng/mL as low and <12 ng/mL as severe deficiency, while 2024 Endocrine Society guidance avoids universal screening/target thresholds for healthy adults. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Confirms the diagnosis, identifies mimics or complications, or establishes a baseline that changes treatment for Osteoporosis. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Calcium, phosphorus, creatinine/eGFR, alkaline phosphatase, 25(OH)D, PTH, TSH/CBC/CMP and secondary-cause labs as indicated.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Confirms the diagnosis, identifies mimics or complications, or establishes a baseline that changes treatment for Osteoporosis. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.

Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Osteoporosis. Source: AACE_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.

Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Osteoporosis. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Intact PTH often about 10-65 pg/mL but assay-specific.: Use as a diagnostic anchor; confirm with local laboratory assay, pregnancy/age/sex context, and acute illness context. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Osteoporosis. Source: AACE_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.

Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Osteoporosis. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- 25(OH)D thresholds vary; many labs flag <20 ng/mL as low and <12 ng/mL as severe deficiency, while 2024 Endocrine Society guidance avoids universal screening/target thresholds for healthy adults.: Use as a diagnostic anchor; confirm with local laboratory assay, pregnancy/age/sex context, and acute illness context. Rationale: Provides diagnostic or safety thresholds that change interpretation and management for Osteoporosis. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- Corrected calcium often about 8.5-10.5 mg/dL; ionized calcium about 1.12-1.32 mmol/L; use local lab.
- Intact PTH often about 10-65 pg/mL but assay-specific.
- DXA T-score: normal >= -1.0; osteopenia -1.0 to -2.5; osteoporosis <= -2.5.
- 25(OH)D thresholds vary; many labs flag <20 ng/mL as low and <12 ng/mL as severe deficiency, while 2024 Endocrine Society guidance avoids universal screening/target thresholds for healthy adults.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- New severe back pain, neurologic symptoms, hip fracture, multiple fragility fractures.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Osteoporosis presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Osteoporosis presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Hip/vertebral fracture, cord/neurologic symptoms with back pain, severe hypercalcemia with dehydration/AKI/confusion, or symptomatic hypocalcemia with seizure/laryngospasm/arrhythmia.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Osteoporosis presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.

Results that change management:
- T-score <= -2.5 or fragility fracture confirms osteoporosis. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Osteoporosis. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Hip/vertebral fracture or very low T-score changes to high/very-high-risk pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Osteoporosis. Source: AACE_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Osteoporosis. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Osteoporosis. Source: AACE_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Fragility fracture, very low T-score, high fracture risk, or secondary cause changes therapy intensity and fall-prevention urgency. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Osteoporosis. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Calcium-PTH pattern, renal involvement, stones, osteoporosis, or severe calcium symptoms changes endocrine/surgical pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Osteoporosis. Source: AACE_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.

## 14. Osteopenia

Category: Bone and Parathyroid Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module osteopenia_v1; validated intent matches: osteopenia_intent_v1 (279)
Guidelines: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; AACE_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Osteopenia. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Osteopenia. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.

Clinical questions:
- Any low-trauma fracture, focal bone pain, height loss, falls, gait instability, back pain, glucocorticoid use, or malabsorption risk? Options: No / Low-trauma fracture / Focal bone pain / Height loss / Falls / Gait instability / Back pain / Glucocorticoid / Malabsorption risk / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Osteopenia needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes fracture risk, calcium/vitamin D/PTH interpretation, imaging threshold, replacement urgency, and fall-prevention planning for Osteopenia. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- What was the menopause or ovarian-insufficiency timing, and are there fragility fracture, vasomotor, genitourinary, or hormone-therapy considerations? Options: No relevant exposure / Medication change / Supplement use / Missed doses / Biotin / Iodine/contrast exposure / Hormone therapy / Recent treatment change / Other ___. Purpose: Defines the patient-specific context needed to interpret endocrine tests, avoid common mimics, and choose the safest next step for Osteopenia. Management: The answer changes fracture risk, calcium/vitamin D/PTH interpretation, imaging threshold, replacement urgency, and fall-prevention planning for Osteopenia. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Any kidney stones, nephrocalcinosis, hematuria, flank pain, recurrent UTIs, polyuria, dehydration, or renal-function changes affecting calcium/PTH interpretation? Options: No / Kidney stones / Nephrocalcinosis / Hematuria / Flank pain / Recurrent UTIs / Polyuria / Dehydration / Renal-function changes affecting calcium/PTH interpretation / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Osteopenia needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes fracture risk, calcium/vitamin D/PTH interpretation, imaging threshold, replacement urgency, and fall-prevention planning for Osteopenia. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Any antiseizure or enzyme-inducing medication use that could affect vitamin D metabolism, bone density, or calcium interpretation? Options: No / Antiseizure / Enzyme-inducing medication use that could affect vitamin D metabolism / Bone density / Calcium interpretation / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Osteopenia therapy unsafe. Management: The answer changes fracture risk, calcium/vitamin D/PTH interpretation, imaging threshold, replacement urgency, and fall-prevention planning for Osteopenia. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Any kidney stones, constipation, polyuria, polydipsia, bone pain, confusion, dehydration, or reduced kidney function? Options: No / Kidney stones / Constipation / Polyuria / Polydipsia / Bone pain / Confusion / Dehydration / Reduced kidney function / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Osteopenia needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes fracture risk, calcium/vitamin D/PTH interpretation, imaging threshold, replacement urgency, and fall-prevention planning for Osteopenia. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.

Conditional history add-ons:
- None.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Test proximal hip flexor strength: Test hip flexion strength against resistance bilaterally while the patient is seated or supine, adapting to pain and safety. Findings: Normal strength / Mild weakness / Needs arms/assistance / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Weakness changes fall risk, severity assessment, and urgency of calcium or vitamin D evaluation. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate focal bone tenderness: Palpate the symptomatic bone or spine area gently for focal tenderness and correlate with trauma, fracture risk, and neurologic symptoms. Findings: No focal tenderness / Focal tenderness / Diffuse tenderness / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Focal tenderness changes fracture concern, imaging need, and treatment urgency. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Observe gait stability if safe: Observe standing and gait only if safe, noting balance, antalgia, assistive-device need, and fall risk. Findings: Stable / Unsteady / Needs assistive device/help / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Unsafe gait changes fall precautions, disposition, and rehabilitation planning. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect spine posture for kyphosis: Inspect standing posture and spinal curvature, noting kyphosis, height-loss concern, or vertebral compression pattern. Findings: No kyphosis/height-loss concern / Kyphosis / Height-loss concern / Unable to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Kyphosis or height-loss concern changes vertebral fracture evaluation and imaging threshold. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Palpate spine for focal tenderness: Palpate the symptomatic bone or spine area gently for focal tenderness and correlate with trauma, fracture risk, and neurologic symptoms. Findings: No focal tenderness / Focal tenderness / Diffuse tenderness / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Focal tenderness changes fracture imaging threshold. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Elicit Chvostek sign: Tap over the facial nerve anterior to the ear and observe for ipsilateral facial twitching, interpreting cautiously because false positives occur. Findings: Negative / Positive / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Positive Chvostek sign changes urgency of calcium testing and replacement. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs. - Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Osteopenia. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Fragility fracture, very low T-score, high fracture risk, or secondary cause changes therapy intensity and fall-prevention urgency. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Osteopenia. Source: AACE_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.
- Calcium-PTH pattern, renal involvement, stones, osteoporosis, or severe calcium symptoms changes endocrine/surgical pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Osteopenia. Source: ENDO_OSTEOPOROSIS_2020.

## 15. Primary Hyperparathyroidism

Category: Bone and Parathyroid Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module primary_hyperparathyroidism_v1; validated intent matches: primary_hyperparathyroidism_intent_v1 (287)
Guidelines: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Primary Hyperparathyroidism. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Primary Hyperparathyroidism. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022.

Conditional history add-ons:
- None.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Test proximal hip flexor strength: Test hip flexion strength against resistance bilaterally while the patient is seated or supine, adapting to pain and safety. Findings: Normal strength / Mild weakness / Needs arms/assistance / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Weakness changes fall risk, severity assessment, and urgency of calcium or vitamin D evaluation. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate focal bone tenderness: Palpate the symptomatic bone or spine area gently for focal tenderness and correlate with trauma, fracture risk, and neurologic symptoms. Findings: No focal tenderness / Focal tenderness / Diffuse tenderness / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Focal tenderness changes fracture concern, imaging need, and treatment urgency. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Observe gait stability if safe: Observe standing and gait only if safe, noting balance, antalgia, assistive-device need, and fall risk. Findings: Stable / Unsteady / Needs assistive device/help / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Unsafe gait changes fall precautions, disposition, and rehabilitation planning. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect spine posture for kyphosis: Inspect standing posture and spinal curvature, noting kyphosis, height-loss concern, or vertebral compression pattern. Findings: No kyphosis/height-loss concern / Kyphosis / Height-loss concern / Unable to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Kyphosis or height-loss concern changes vertebral fracture evaluation and imaging threshold. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy and urgency of hypercalcemia management. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

- Palpate spine for focal tenderness: Palpate the symptomatic bone or spine area gently for focal tenderness and correlate with trauma, fracture risk, and neurologic symptoms. Findings: Negative / Positive / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Positive Chvostek sign changes urgency of calcium testing and replacement. Findings: Negative / Positive / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Positive Trousseau sign changes urgency of calcium replacement and monitoring. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment blood pressure cuff

Diagnostic workup and reference values:
- Repeat albumin-corrected/ionized calcium with intact PTH.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: Corrected calcium often about 8.5-10.5 mg/dL; ionized calcium about 1.12-1.32 mmol/L; use local lab. Intact PTH often about 10-65 pg/mL but assay-specific. DXA T-score: normal >= -1.0; osteopenia -1.0 to -2.5; osteoporosis <= -2.5. 25(OH)D thresholds vary; many labs flag <20 ng/mL as low and <12 ng/mL as severe deficiency, while 2024 Endocrine Society guidance avoids universal screening/target thresholds for healthy adults. PHPT: high calcium with elevated or inappropriately normal PTH; FHH often Ca/Cr clearance ratio <0.01 but overlap exists. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- Corrected calcium often about 8.5-10.5 mg/dL; ionized calcium about 1.12-1.32 mmol/L; use local lab.
- Intact PTH often about 10-65 pg/mL but assay-specific.
- DXA T-score: normal >= -1.0; osteopenia -1.0 to -2.5; osteoporosis <= -2.5.
- 25(OH)D thresholds vary; many labs flag <20 ng/mL as low and <12 ng/mL as severe deficiency, while 2024 Endocrine Society guidance avoids universal screening/target thresholds for healthy adults.
- PHPT: high calcium with elevated or inappropriately normal PTH; FHH often Ca/Cr clearance ratio <0.01 but overlap exists.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Severe hypercalcemia, dehydration, AKI, confusion, pancreatitis.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Primary Hyperparathyroidism presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Primary Hyperparathyroidism presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022.
- Hip/vertebral fracture, cord/neurologic symptoms with back pain, severe hypercalcemia with dehydration/AKI/confusion, or symptomatic hypocalcemia with seizure/laryngospasm/arrhythmia.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Primary Hyperparathyroidism presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022.

Results that change management:
- Ca >1 mg/dL above ULN, osteoporosis/fracture, stones, reduced renal function, or age criteria can change to surgical pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Primary Hyperparathyroidism. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Primary Hyperparathyroidism. Source: PHPT_WORKSHOP_2022.

Diagnostic workup and reference values:

Intact PTH often about 10-65 pg/mL but assay-specific. DXA T-score: normal >= -1.0; osteopenia -1.0 to -2.5; osteoporosis <= -2.5. 25(OH)D thresholds vary; many labs flag <20 ng/mL as low and <12 ng/mL as severe deficiency, while 2024 Endocrine Society guidance avoids universal screening/target thresholds for healthy adults. Hypoparathyroidism: low calcium with low or inappropriately normal PTH, often high phosphorus. Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- Corrected calcium often about 8.5-10.5 mg/dL; ionized calcium about 1.12-1.32 mmol/L; use local lab.
- Intact PTH often about 10-65 pg/mL but assay-specific.
- DXA T-score: normal >= -1.0; osteopenia -1.0 to -2.5; osteoporosis <= -2.5.
- 25(OH)D thresholds vary; many labs flag <20 ng/mL as low and <12 ng/mL as severe deficiency, while 2024 Endocrine Society guidance avoids universal screening/target thresholds for healthy adults.
- Hypoparathyroidism: low calcium with low or inappropriately normal PTH, often high phosphorus.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Seizure, laryngospasm, arrhythmia/QT prolongation, severe symptomatic hypocalcemia.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypoparathyroidism presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: HYPOPARA_TASK_FORCE_2022.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypoparathyroidism presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: HYPOPARA_TASK_FORCE_2022.
- Hip/vertebral fracture, cord/neurologic symptoms with back pain, severe hypercalcemia with dehydration/AKI/confusion, or symptomatic hypocalcemia with seizure/laryngospasm/arrhythmia.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypoparathyroidism presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: HYPOPARA_TASK_FORCE_2022.

Results that change management:
- Symptomatic or severe hypocalcemia changes to urgent calcium replacement and ECG monitoring. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypoparathyroidism. Source: HYPOPARA_TASK_FORCE_2022.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypoparathyroidism. Source: HYPOPARA_TASK_FORCE_2022.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypoparathyroidism. Source: HYPOPARA_TASK_FORCE_2022.
- Fragility fracture, very low T-score, high fracture risk, or secondary cause changes therapy intensity and fall-prevention urgency. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypoparathyroidism. Source: HYPOPARA_TASK_FORCE_2022.
- Calcium-PTH pattern, renal involvement, stones, osteoporosis, or severe calcium symptoms changes endocrine/surgical pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypoparathyroidism. Source: HYPOPARA_TASK_FORCE_2022.

## 17. Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia

Category: Bone and Parathyroid Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module vitamin_d_deficiency_osteomalacia_v1; validated intent matches: vitamin_d_deficiency_osteomalacia_intent_v1 (405)
Guidelines: ENDO_VITD_2024; NIH_VITD_FACTSHEET

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.

Clinical questions:
- Do you have trouble rising from a chair, climbing stairs, lifting overhead, or getting up from the floor? Options: Trouble rising from chair / Climbing stairs / Lifting overhead / Getting up from the floor / Other ___. Purpose: Defines the patient-specific context needed to interpret endocrine tests, avoid common mimics, and choose the safest next step for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Management: The answer changes the leading Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia pathway by refining severity, mimics, confirmatory testing, treatment safety, and follow-up timing. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.
- Any malabsorption, bariatric surgery, inflammatory bowel disease, celiac disease, pancreatic disease, or chronic diarrhea affecting nutrient or medication absorption? Options: No / Malabsorption / Bariatric surgery / Inflammatory bowel disease / Celiac disease / Pancreatic disease / Chronic diarrhea affecting nutrient / Medication absorption / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia therapy unsafe. Management: The answer changes fracture risk, calcium/vitamin D/PTH interpretation, imaging threshold, replacement urgency, and fall-prevention planning for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.
- Any chronic kidney disease, liver disease, malabsorption, bariatric surgery, or other condition that could alter vitamin D, calcium, phosphorus, or PTH interpretation? Options: No / Chronic kidney disease / Liver disease / Malabsorption / Bariatric surgery / Other condition that could alter vitamin D / Calcium / Phosphorus / PTH interpretation / Other ___. Purpose: Defines the patient-specific context needed to interpret endocrine tests, avoid common mimics, and choose the safest next step for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Management: The answer changes fracture risk, calcium/vitamin D/PTH interpretation, imaging threshold, replacement urgency, and fall-prevention planning for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.
- Any antiseizure or enzyme-inducing medication use that could affect vitamin D metabolism, bone density, or calcium interpretation? Options: No / Antiseizure / Enzyme-inducing medication use that could affect vitamin D metabolism / Bone density / Calcium interpretation / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia therapy unsafe. Management: The answer changes fracture risk, calcium/vitamin D/PTH interpretation, imaging threshold, replacement urgency, and fall-prevention planning for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.
- Any kidney stones, nephrocalcinosis, hematuria, flank pain, recurrent UTIs, polyuria, dehydration, or renal-function changes affecting calcium/PTH interpretation? Options: No / Kidney stones / Nephrocalcinosis / Hematuria / Flank pain / Recurrent UTIs / Polyuria / Dehydration / Renal-function changes affecting calcium/PTH interpretation / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes fracture risk, calcium/vitamin D/PTH interpretation, imaging threshold, replacement urgency, and fall-prevention planning for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.

Conditional history add-ons:
- None.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Test proximal hip flexor strength: Test hip flexion strength against resistance bilaterally while the patient is seated or supine, adapting to pain and safety. Findings: Normal strength / Mild weakness / Needs arms/assistance / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Weakness changes fall risk, severity assessment, and urgency of calcium or vitamin D evaluation. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Palpate focal bone tenderness: Palpate the symptomatic bone or spine area gently for focal tenderness and correlate with trauma, fracture risk, and neurologic symptoms. Findings: No focal tenderness / Focal tenderness / Diffuse tenderness / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Focal tenderness changes fracture concern, imaging need, and treatment urgency. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Observe gait stability if safe: Observe standing and gait only if safe, noting balance, antalgia, assistive-device need, and fall risk. Findings: Stable / Unsteady / Needs assistive device/help / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Unsafe gait changes fall precautions, disposition, and rehabilitation planning. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect spine posture for kyphosis: Inspect standing posture and spinal curvature, noting kyphosis, height-loss concern, or vertebral compression pattern. Findings: No kyphosis/height-loss concern / Kyphosis / Height-loss concern / Unable to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Kyphosis or height-loss concern changes vertebral fracture evaluation and imaging threshold. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Elicit Chvostek sign: Tap over the facial nerve anterior to the ear and observe for ipsilateral facial twitching, interpreting cautiously because false positives occur. Findings: Negative / Positive / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Positive neuromuscular irritability changes urgency of calcium testing and treatment. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Elicit Trousseau sign: Inflate a blood-pressure cuff above systolic pressure for up to three minutes if safe and observe for carpopedal spasm. Findings: Negative / Positive / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: hypocalcemia, osteomalacia/osteoporosis complication, fracture risk, or fall risk Management: Positive carpopedal spasm changes urgency of calcium replacement and monitoring. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment blood pressure cuff

- Intact PTH often about 10-65 pg/mL but assay-specific.
- DXA T-score: normal >= -1.0; osteopenia -1.0 to -2.5; osteoporosis <= -2.5.
- 25(OH)D thresholds vary; many labs flag <20 ng/mL as low and <12 ng/mL as severe deficiency, while 2024 Endocrine Society guidance avoids universal screening/target thresholds for healthy adults.
- Osteomalacia pattern can include low/normal calcium, low phosphorus, high alkaline phosphatase, and secondary high PTH.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Severe hypocalcemia symptoms, fracture, profound weakness, malabsorption/high-risk state.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.
- Hip/vertebral fracture, cord/neurologic symptoms with back pain, severe hypercalcemia with dehydration/AKI/confusion, or symptomatic hypocalcemia with seizure/laryngospasm/arrhythmia.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.

Results that change management:
- Low 25(OH)D with symptoms or osteomalacia labs changes from prevention advice to treatment and etiology evaluation. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Source: NIH_VITD_FACTSHEET.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.
- Fragility fracture, very low T-score, high fracture risk, or secondary cause changes therapy intensity and fall-prevention urgency. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Source: NIH_VITD_FACTSHEET.
- Calcium-PTH pattern, renal involvement, stones, osteoporosis, or severe calcium symptoms changes endocrine/surgical pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Vitamin D Deficiency / Osteomalacia. Source: ENDO_VITD_2024.

## 18. Adrenal Insufficiency

Category: Adrenal Gland Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module adrenal_insufficiency_v1; validated intent matches: adrenal_insufficiency_intent_v1 (287); addisons_disease_intent_v1 (88)
Guidelines: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Adrenal Insufficiency. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Adrenal Insufficiency. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Measure orthostatic blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Orthostasis changes crisis concern, fluid strategy, and hormone replacement urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Adrenal Insufficiency. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Inspect oral mucosa for hyperpigmentation: Inspect oral mucosa, palmar creases, scars, and sun-protected skin for diffuse or patchy hyperpigmentation. Findings: Absent / Oral/palmar hyperpigmentation / Diffuse or scar hyperpigmentation / Unable to assess. Target: primary adrenal insufficiency, ACTH excess pattern, or congenital adrenal hyperplasia clue Management: Hyperpigmentation supports primary adrenal insufficiency or ACTH excess and changes ACTH, antibody, renin/aldosterone, or steroid-replacement interpretation. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dry mucous membranes change adrenal-crisis severity assessment, fluid urgency, and stress-dose steroid planning. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Test chair-rise strength: Ask the patient to rise from a chair without using arms if safe, observing proximal strength and need for assistance. Findings: Normal strength / Mild weakness / Needs arms/assistance / Unable/unsafe to assess. Target: clinically important weakness, adrenal-crisis severity, or functional impairment Management: Clinically important weakness changes crisis severity, fall risk, and monitored-care threshold. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Palpate abdomen for tenderness: Inspect and palpate the abdomen gently, localizing tenderness and stopping if guarding, rebound, or severe pain occurs. Findings: Nontender / Tender / Guarding / Rebound/peritoneal concern / Unable to assess. Target: abdominal complication, endocrine crisis mimic, or precipitating illness Management: Tenderness changes adrenal crisis severity and mimic evaluation. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Diagnostic workup and reference values:
- 8 AM cortisol and ACTH.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: 8 AM cortisol <3 ug/dL strongly suggests adrenal insufficiency; >15-18 ug/dL often makes it unlikely, context dependent. Cosyntropin peak cortisol <18 ug/dL is a traditional abnormal cutoff; modern assays may use about 14-15 ug/dL. Sodium about 135-145 mmol/L; potassium about 3.5-5.0 mmol/L. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- 8 AM cortisol <3 ug/dL strongly suggests adrenal insufficiency; >15-18 ug/dL often makes it unlikely, context dependent.
- Cosyntropin peak cortisol <18 ug/dL is a traditional abnormal cutoff; modern assays may use about 14-15 ug/dL.
- Sodium about 135-145 mmol/L; potassium about 3.5-5.0 mmol/L.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Shock, vomiting/dehydration, hypoglycemia, severe hyponatremia/hyperkalemia, altered mental status.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Adrenal Insufficiency presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Adrenal Insufficiency presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Adrenal crisis, shock, severe vomiting/dehydration, hypoglycemia, severe hyperkalemia/hyponatremia, hypertensive crisis, arrhythmia, stroke/ACS symptoms, psychosis, infection, or VTE.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Adrenal Insufficiency presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.

Results that change management:
- Suspected adrenal crisis should be treated urgently; do not delay hydrocortisone for testing if unstable. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Adrenal Insufficiency. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Adrenal Insufficiency. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Adrenal Insufficiency. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Suspected adrenal crisis is treated immediately with stress-dose steroids and fluids; testing must not delay treatment when unstable. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Adrenal Insufficiency. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Marked metanephrine elevation, suppressed renin with high aldosterone, or confirmed hypercortisolism changes to specialty localization/subtyping and perioperative planning. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Adrenal Insufficiency. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.

Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.

- None.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Inspect oral mucosa for hyperpigmentation: Inspect oral mucosa, palmar creases, scars, and sun-protected skin for diffuse or patchy hyperpigmentation. Findings: Absent / Oral/palmar hyperpigmentation / Diffuse or scar hyperpigmentation / Unable to assess. Target: primary adrenal insufficiency, ACTH excess pattern, or congenital adrenal hyperplasia clue Management: Hyperpigmentation supports primary adrenal insufficiency or ACTH excess and changes ACTH, antibody, renin/aldosterone, or steroid-replacement interpretation. Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- 8 AM cortisol <3 ug/dL strongly suggests adrenal insufficiency; >15-18 ug/dL often makes it unlikely, context dependent.
- Cosyntropin peak cortisol <18 ug/dL is a traditional abnormal cutoff; modern assays may use about 14-15 ug/dL.
- Sodium about 135-145 mmol/L; potassium about 3.5-5.0 mmol/L.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Adrenal crisis, severe hyperkalemia, shock, infection.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Addison's Disease presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Addison's Disease presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Adrenal crisis, shock, severe vomiting/dehydration, hypoglycemia, severe hyperkalemia/hyponatremia, hypertensive crisis, arrhythmia, stroke/ACS symptoms, psychosis, infection, or VTE.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Addison's Disease presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.

Results that change management:
- High ACTH plus low cortisol confirms primary pattern; mineralocorticoid deficiency changes therapy to fludrocortisone/salt guidance. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Addison's Disease. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Addison's Disease. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Addison's Disease. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Suspected adrenal crisis is treated immediately with stress-dose steroids and fluids; testing must not delay treatment when unstable. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Addison's Disease. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.
- Marked metanephrine elevation, suppressed renin with high aldosterone, or confirmed hypercortisolism changes to specialty localization/subtyping and perioperative planning. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Addison's Disease. Source: ES_ADRENAL_INSUFFICIENCY_2016.

## 20. Cushing's Syndrome

Category: Adrenal Gland Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module cushings_syndrome_v1; validated intent matches: cushings_syndrome_intent_v1 (287)
Guidelines: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008; ES_CUSHING_TREATMENT_2015; ESE_ADRENAL_INCIDENTALOMA_2023

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Cushing's Syndrome. Source: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Cushing's Syndrome. Source: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008.
- Measure orthostatic blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Orthostasis changes crisis concern, fluid strategy, and hormone replacement urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Cushing's Syndrome. Source: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008.

Rationale: Identifies dangerous Cushing's Syndrome presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008.
- Adrenal crisis, shock, severe vomiting/dehydration, hypoglycemia, severe hyperkalemia/hyponatremia, hypertensive crisis, arrhythmia, stroke/ACS symptoms, psychosis, infection, or VTE.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Cushing's Syndrome presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008.

Results that change management:
- Abnormal screening plus convincing phenotype triggers confirmatory/endocrine pathway; ACTH directs adrenal vs ACTH-dependent workup. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Cushing's Syndrome. Source: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Cushing's Syndrome. Source: ES_CUSHING_TREATMENT_2015.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Cushing's Syndrome. Source: ESE_ADRENAL_INCIDENTALOMA_2023.
- Suspected adrenal crisis is treated immediately with stress-dose steroids and fluids; testing must not delay treatment when unstable. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Cushing's Syndrome. Source: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008.
- Marked metanephrine elevation, suppressed renin with high aldosterone, or confirmed hypercortisolism changes to specialty localization/subtyping and perioperative planning. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Cushing's Syndrome. Source: ES_CUSHING_TREATMENT_2015.

Core physical exam maneuvers:

Target: catecholamine-related tachyarrhythmia or severe hypertension complication Management: Arrhythmia changes monitoring urgency and perioperative safety planning. Source: ES_PHEO_PPGL_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment stethoscope
- Inspect for diaphoresis: Inspect the named area directly, comparing sides when relevant and documenting presence, absence, severity, and inability to assess. Findings: Absent / Present / Profuse/during spell / Unable to assess. Target: catecholamine excess, adrenergic spell severity, or autonomic instability Management: Diaphoresis during a spell changes urgency, monitoring, and catecholamine-excess framing. Source: ES_PHEO_PPGL_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Observe outstretched-hands tremor: Ask the patient to extend both arms and spread fingers; observe for fine tremor and functional impact. Findings: No tremor / Fine tremor / Coarse tremor / Functionally limiting tremor / Unable to assess. Target: catecholamine excess, adrenergic spell severity, or autonomic instability Management: Tremor supports adrenergic physiology and changes monitoring and medication-safety planning. Source: ES_PHEO_PPGL_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Target: abdominal complication, endocrine crisis mimic, or precipitating illness Management: Tenderness changes adrenal crisis severity and mimic evaluation. Source: ES_PHEO_PPGL_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs. Source: ES_PHEO_PPGL_2014; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

## 23. Congenital Adrenal Hyperplasia (CAH)

Category: Adrenal Gland Disorders

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Congenital Adrenal Hyperplasia (CAH). Source: ES_CAH_2018.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Congenital Adrenal Hyperplasia (CAH). Source: ES_CAH_2018.
- Measure orthostatic blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Orthostasis changes crisis concern, fluid strategy, and hormone replacement urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Congenital Adrenal Hyperplasia (CAH). Source: ES_CAH_2018.

Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Polycystic Ovary Syndrome (PCOS). Source: PCOS_GUIDELINE_2023.

Rationale: Quantifies anthropometric and cardiometabolic risk so abnormal values can change diagnostic criteria, treatment selection, dosing context, or prevention intensity for Polycystic Ovary Syndrome (PCOS). Red flags:
- Rapid virilization, very high testosterone/DHEAS, pelvic mass, severe abnormal uterine bleeding.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. - Positive pregnancy with pain/bleeding, rapid virilization, tumor-range androgens, severe abnormal bleeding, visual symptoms/headache, testicular mass, hard breast mass, or priapism.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Polycystic Ovary Syndrome (PCOS) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: PCOS_GUIDELINE_2023.

Results that change management:
- Tumor-range androgens or rapid virilization changes to urgent imaging/endocrine evaluation. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Polycystic Ovary Syndrome (PCOS). Source: PCOS_GUIDELINE_2023.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Polycystic Ovary Syndrome (PCOS). Source: PCOS_GUIDELINE_2023.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Polycystic Ovary Syndrome (PCOS). Source: PCOS_GUIDELINE_2023.
- Pregnancy, fertility intent, rapid virilization, tumor-range hormones, or pituitary symptoms changes medication safety, imaging urgency, and referral pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Polycystic Ovary Syndrome (PCOS). Source: PCOS_GUIDELINE_2023.
- Biochemical hypogonadism, POI, hyperprolactinemia, PCOS, or thyroid disease changes counseling, bone/cardiometabolic prevention, and treatment selection. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Polycystic Ovary Syndrome (PCOS). Source: PCOS_GUIDELINE_2023.

## 25. Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men)

Category: Reproductive and Gonadal Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module hypogonadism_v1; validated intent matches: hypogonadism_intent_v1 (381)
Guidelines: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018; AUA_TESTOSTERONE_2024

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- Measure body mass index: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. BMI changes PCOS, hypogonadism, infertility, menopause, and cardiometabolic risk framing. Rationale: Quantifies anthropometric and cardiometabolic risk so abnormal values can change diagnostic criteria, treatment selection, dosing context, or prevention intensity for Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- Prolactin upper limit often about 20 ng/mL in men and 25 ng/mL in women, but lab, pregnancy, lactation, and macroprolactin matter.
- Male total testosterone should be early morning and repeated; lower limit often around 264-300 ng/dL depending assay.
- IGF-1, LH/FSH, estradiol, AMH, and pediatric growth labs require age/sex/puberty-specific ranges.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- New severe headache/vision loss, very low T with low/normal LH/FSH, testicular mass, infertility priority.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- Positive pregnancy with pain/bleeding, rapid virilization, tumor-range androgens, severe abnormal bleeding, visual symptoms/headache, testicular mass, hard breast mass, or priapism.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.

Results that change management:
- Fertility plans change away from exogenous testosterone; pituitary signs trigger MRI/endocrine referral. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men). Source: AUA_TESTOSTERONE_2024.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- Pregnancy, fertility intent, rapid virilization, tumor-range hormones, or pituitary symptoms changes medication safety, imaging urgency, and referral pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men). Source: AUA_TESTOSTERONE_2024.
- Biochemical hypogonadism, POI, hyperprolactinemia, PCOS, or thyroid disease changes counseling, bone/cardiometabolic prevention, and treatment selection. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypogonadism (Low Testosterone in Men). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
