Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Menopause / Premature Ovarian Insufficiency. Source: ESHRE_POI_2024.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Menopause / Premature Ovarian Insufficiency. Source: ESHRE_POI_2024.
- Measure body mass index: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. BMI changes PCOS, hypogonadism, infertility, menopause, and cardiometabolic risk framing. Rationale: Quantifies anthropometric and cardiometabolic risk so abnormal values can change diagnostic criteria, treatment selection, dosing context, or prevention intensity for Menopause / Premature Ovarian Insufficiency. Source: ESHRE_POI_2024.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Inspect acne distribution: Inspect the relevant androgen-sensitive areas respectfully and document distribution, severity, and signs of virilization. Findings: Absent/minimal / Inflammatory acne / Severe/nodulocystic / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Inflammatory acne supports hyperandrogenism and changes androgen testing threshold. Source: ESHRE_POI_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect terminal hair distribution: Inspect the relevant androgen-sensitive areas respectfully and document distribution, severity, and signs of virilization. Findings: Expected distribution / Mild excess / Marked excess / Virilization concern / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Terminal hair pattern changes hyperandrogenism grading and need for androgen evaluation. Source: ESHRE_POI_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect thyroid gland: Inspect and palpate the thyroid from in front or behind while the patient swallows, noting size, tenderness, asymmetry, nodules, fixation, or bruit if auscultated. Findings: Normal size / Goiter / Nodule/asymmetry / Tender / Fixed/hard / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid structural disease, compressive features, or thyroid inflammatory/autoimmune pattern Management: Goiter changes thyroid testing interpretation and differential diagnosis. Source: ESHRE_POI_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect for galactorrhea: Inspect for spontaneous discharge and, only when clinically appropriate, gently express from the areola toward the nipple while preserving privacy and consent. Findings: Absent / Spontaneous discharge / Expressible discharge / Bloody/unilateral discharge / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Galactorrhea changes prolactin testing and pituitary evaluation threshold. Source: ESHRE_POI_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Suspicious breast findings change endocrine versus breast-mass pathway. Source: ESHRE_POI_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs. Source: ESHRE_POI_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Measure testicular volume: Estimate testicular volume with orchidometer when available or careful exam, documenting asymmetry, tenderness, or mass separately. Findings: Expected volume / Small bilaterally / Asymmetric/mass concern / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Small testes change primary versus central hypogonadism framing and fertility counseling. Source: AUA_ED_2018; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment orchidometer optional
- Inspect breast tissue: Inspect and palpate breast tissue to distinguish glandular tissue from adiposity and to identify discrete mass, tenderness, or discharge. Findings: No glandular tissue / Tender glandular tissue / Discrete mass / Nipple discharge/skin change / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: True glandular tissue or suspicious mass changes endocrine versus breast-mass pathway. Source: AUA_ED_2018; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect body hair distribution: Inspect the relevant androgen-sensitive areas respectfully and document distribution, severity, and signs of virilization. Findings: Expected distribution / Reduced androgen-dependent hair / Excess/virilizing pattern / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Reduced androgen-dependent hair supports hypogonadism and changes diagnostic framing. Source: AUA_ED_2018; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Findings: Absent / Spontaneous discharge / Expressible discharge / Bloody/unilateral discharge / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Galactorrhea changes prolactin and pituitary testing threshold. Source: AUA_ED_2018; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Source: AUA_ED_2018; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Diagnostic workup and reference values:
- Morning total testosterone.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: Prolactin upper limit often about 20 ng/mL in men and 25 ng/mL in women, but lab, pregnancy, lactation, and macroprolactin matter. Male total testosterone should be early morning and repeated; lower limit often around 264-300 ng/dL depending assay. IGF-1, LH/FSH, estradiol, AMH, and pediatric growth labs require age/sex/puberty-specific ranges. A1c: normal <5.7%; prediabetes 5.7-6.4%; diabetes >=6.5%. Fasting plasma glucose: normal <100 mg/dL; prediabetes 100-125; diabetes >=126. 2-hour 75-g OGTT: normal <140 mg/dL; prediabetes 140-199; diabetes >=200. Random plasma glucose >=200 mg/dL with classic symptoms supports diabetes diagnosis. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. - Random plasma glucose >=200 mg/dL with classic symptoms supports diabetes diagnosis.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:

Rationale: Identifies dangerous Erectile Dysfunction (Endocrine-related) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: AUA_ED_2018.

Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Erectile Dysfunction (Endocrine-related). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.

Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Erectile Dysfunction (Endocrine-related). Source: AUA_TESTOSTERONE_2024.

Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Erectile Dysfunction (Endocrine-related). Source: AUA_ED_2018.
- Biochemical hypogonadism, POI, hyperprolactinemia, PCOS, or thyroid disease changes counseling, bone/cardiometabolic prevention, and treatment selection. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Erectile Dysfunction (Endocrine-related). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.

## 28. Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation)

Category: Reproductive and Gonadal Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module amenorrhea_v1; validated intent matches: amenorrhea_intent_v1 (372)
Guidelines: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Measure body mass index: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. BMI changes PCOS, hypogonadism, infertility, menopause, and cardiometabolic risk framing. Rationale: Quantifies anthropometric and cardiometabolic risk so abnormal values can change diagnostic criteria, treatment selection, dosing context, or prevention intensity for Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.

Findings: Expected distribution / Mild excess / Marked excess / Virilization concern / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Terminal hair pattern changes hyperandrogenism grading and need for androgen evaluation. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect neck for acanthosis: Inspect the named area directly, comparing sides when relevant and documenting presence, absence, severity, and inability to assess. Findings: Absent / Mild neck folds / Marked neck/axillary involvement / Unable to assess. Target: insulin resistance or cardiometabolic risk phenotype Management: Acanthosis changes metabolic-risk framing and diabetes screening urgency. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect thyroid gland: Inspect and palpate the thyroid from in front or behind while the patient swallows, noting size, tenderness, asymmetry, nodules, fixation, or bruit if auscultated. Findings: Normal size / Goiter / Nodule/asymmetry / Tender / Fixed/hard / Unable to assess. Target: thyroid structural disease, compressive features, or thyroid inflammatory/autoimmune pattern Management: Goiter changes thyroid testing interpretation and differential diagnosis. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect for galactorrhea: Inspect for spontaneous discharge and, only when clinically appropriate, gently express from the areola toward the nipple while preserving privacy and consent. Findings: Absent / Spontaneous discharge / Expressible discharge / Bloody/unilateral discharge / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Galactorrhea changes prolactin testing and pituitary evaluation threshold. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Inspect for clitoromegaly: Inspect the relevant androgen-sensitive areas respectfully and document distribution, severity, and signs of virilization. Findings: Absent / Present/possible / Rapid virilization concern / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Virilization changes urgency of androgen tumor evaluation. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect breast tissue: Inspect and palpate breast tissue to distinguish glandular tissue from adiposity and to identify discrete mass, tenderness, or discharge. Findings: No glandular tissue / Tender glandular tissue / Discrete mass / Nipple discharge/skin change / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Suspicious breast findings change endocrine versus breast-mass pathway. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Diagnostic workup and reference values:
- Pregnancy test first.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: Prolactin upper limit often about 20 ng/mL in men and 25 ng/mL in women, but lab, pregnancy, lactation, and macroprolactin matter. Male total testosterone should be early morning and repeated; lower limit often around 264-300 ng/dL depending assay. IGF-1, LH/FSH, estradiol, AMH, and pediatric growth labs require age/sex/puberty-specific ranges. TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context. Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay. T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Confirms the diagnosis, identifies mimics or complications, or establishes a baseline that changes treatment for Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- Prolactin upper limit often about 20 ng/mL in men and 25 ng/mL in women, but lab, pregnancy, lactation, and macroprolactin matter.
- Male total testosterone should be early morning and repeated; lower limit often around 264-300 ng/dL depending assay.
- IGF-1, LH/FSH, estradiol, AMH, and pediatric growth labs require age/sex/puberty-specific ranges.
- TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context.
- Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay.
- T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Positive pregnancy with pain/bleeding, visual loss/headache, rapid virilization, vital sign instability/eating disorder.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Positive pregnancy with pain/bleeding, rapid virilization, tumor-range androgens, severe abnormal bleeding, visual symptoms/headache, testicular mass, hard breast mass, or priapism.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.

Results that change management:
- FSH/E2 pattern separates ovarian failure from central/hypothalamic causes and changes imaging/referral. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Pregnancy, fertility intent, rapid virilization, tumor-range hormones, or pituitary symptoms changes medication safety, imaging urgency, and referral pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Biochemical hypogonadism, POI, hyperprolactinemia, PCOS, or thyroid disease changes counseling, bone/cardiometabolic prevention, and treatment selection. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Amenorrhea (Absence of menstruation). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.

## 29. Infertility (Hormonal causes)

Category: Reproductive and Gonadal Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module infertility_v1; validated intent matches: infertility_intent_v1 (368)
Guidelines: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024; PCOS_GUIDELINE_2023; ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Infertility (Hormonal causes). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Infertility (Hormonal causes). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Measure body mass index: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. BMI changes PCOS, hypogonadism, infertility, menopause, and cardiometabolic risk framing. Rationale: Quantifies anthropometric and cardiometabolic risk so abnormal values can change diagnostic criteria, treatment selection, dosing context, or prevention intensity for Infertility (Hormonal causes). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- Prolactin upper limit often about 20 ng/mL in men and 25 ng/mL in women, but lab, pregnancy, lactation, and macroprolactin matter.
- Male total testosterone should be early morning and repeated; lower limit often around 264-300 ng/dL depending assay.
- IGF-1, LH/FSH, estradiol, AMH, and pediatric growth labs require age/sex/puberty-specific ranges.
- TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context.
- Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay.
- T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Amenorrhea with visual symptoms, POI <40, severe hyperandrogenism, recurrent pregnancy loss needing specialist workup.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Infertility (Hormonal causes) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Infertility (Hormonal causes) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Positive pregnancy with pain/bleeding, rapid virilization, tumor-range androgens, severe abnormal bleeding, visual symptoms/headache, testicular mass, hard breast mass, or priapism.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Infertility (Hormonal causes) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.

Results that change management:
- Anovulation, thyroid/prolactin abnormality, POI pattern, or male factor changes treatment/referral. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Infertility (Hormonal causes). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Infertility (Hormonal causes). Source: PCOS_GUIDELINE_2023.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Infertility (Hormonal causes). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- Pregnancy, fertility intent, rapid virilization, tumor-range hormones, or pituitary symptoms changes medication safety, imaging urgency, and referral pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Infertility (Hormonal causes). Source: ASRM_AMENORRHEA_2024.
- Biochemical hypogonadism, POI, hyperprolactinemia, PCOS, or thyroid disease changes counseling, bone/cardiometabolic prevention, and treatment selection. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Infertility (Hormonal causes). Source: PCOS_GUIDELINE_2023.

## 30. Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue)

Category: Reproductive and Gonadal Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module gynecomastia_v1; validated intent matches: gynecomastia_intent_v1 (385)
Guidelines: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018; AUA_TESTOSTERONE_2024; ES_HYPERPROLACTINEMIA_2011

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- Measure body mass index: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. BMI changes PCOS, hypogonadism, infertility, menopause, and cardiometabolic risk framing. Rationale: Quantifies anthropometric and cardiometabolic risk so abnormal values can change diagnostic criteria, treatment selection, dosing context, or prevention intensity for Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.

Clinical questions:
- How long has breast tissue enlargement or tenderness been present, is it unilateral or bilateral, and have rapid growth, discrete mass, skin change, or nipple discharge occurred? Options: Breast enlargement duration / Breast tenderness duration / Unilateral breast enlargement / Bilateral / Rapid growth / Discrete mass / Skin change / Nipple discharge / Other ___. Purpose: Defines the patient-specific context needed to interpret endocrine tests, avoid common mimics, and choose the safest next step for Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue). Management: The answer changes the leading Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue) pathway by refining severity, mimics, confirmatory testing, treatment safety, and follow-up timing. Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- Any breast tenderness, discrete mass, nipple discharge, testicular pain or mass, fertility change, libido change, medication exposure, liver/kidney disease, alcohol, or cannabis use? Options: Not possible / Possible / Known pregnant/postpartum / Timing/dating known / Unknown / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue) therapy unsafe. Management: The answer changes reproductive-axis localization, pregnancy or fertility safety, androgen/prolactin/gonadal testing, and referral urgency for Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- Any change in libido, morning erections, erectile function, ejaculation, orgasm, fertility goals, or testicular symptoms? Options: Not possible / Possible / Known pregnant/postpartum / Timing/dating known / Unknown / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue) therapy unsafe. Management: The answer changes reproductive-axis localization, pregnancy or fertility safety, androgen/prolactin/gonadal testing, and referral urgency for Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.
- How has height or growth velocity changed compared with prior measurements, family height pattern, and puberty timing? Options: Height/growth change / Growth velocity changed compared with prior measurements / Family height pattern / Puberty timing / Other ___. Purpose: Defines the patient-specific context needed to interpret endocrine tests, avoid common mimics, and choose the safest next step for Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue). Management: The answer changes pregnancy or reproductive safety, assay interpretation, medication choice, imaging timing, or referral urgency for Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.

Conditional history add-ons:
- Any weight loss, eating restriction, intense exercise, psychosocial stress, or change in energy balance that could suppress reproductive hormones? Options: Unknown / Yes / No / Other. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue) needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes cardiometabolic risk stratification, prevention intensity, complication screening, and follow-up interval for Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue). Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.

Management: The answer changes the leading Gynecomastia (Enlarged male breast tissue) pathway by refining severity, mimics, confirmatory testing, treatment safety, and follow-up timing. Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Measure testicular volume: Estimate testicular volume with orchidometer when available or careful exam, documenting asymmetry, tenderness, or mass separately. Findings: Expected volume / Small bilaterally / Asymmetric/mass concern / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Small testes change primary versus central hypogonadism framing and fertility counseling. Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment orchidometer optional
- Inspect breast tissue: Inspect and palpate breast tissue to distinguish glandular tissue from adiposity and to identify discrete mass, tenderness, or discharge. Findings: No glandular tissue / Tender glandular tissue / Discrete mass / Nipple discharge/skin change / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: True glandular tissue or suspicious mass changes endocrine versus breast-mass pathway. Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect body hair distribution: Inspect the relevant androgen-sensitive areas respectfully and document distribution, severity, and signs of virilization. Findings: Expected distribution / Reduced androgen-dependent hair / Excess/virilizing pattern / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Reduced androgen-dependent hair supports hypogonadism and changes diagnostic framing. Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Inspect for galactorrhea: Inspect for spontaneous discharge and, only when clinically appropriate, gently express from the areola toward the nipple while preserving privacy and consent. Findings: Absent / Spontaneous discharge / Expressible discharge / Bloody/unilateral discharge / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Galactorrhea changes prolactin and pituitary testing threshold. Source: ES_TESTOSTERONE_2018; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs. - Prolactin upper limit often about 20 ng/mL in men and 25 ng/mL in women, but lab, pregnancy, lactation, and macroprolactin matter.

Options: Reliable water access / Thirst/intake limits hydration / Intake / Mental status limiting safe hydration / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Prolactinoma (Benign pituitary tumor) needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The pattern changes fluid-sodium interpretation, urine testing priority, desmopressin or hydration safety, and monitoring needs for Prolactinoma (Benign pituitary tumor). - None.

- Test confrontation visual fields: Test each eye separately by confrontation, comparing peripheral fields with the examiner's field while the patient fixes on a central target. Target: pituitary/sellar mass effect or cranial nerve involvement Management: Visual field loss changes urgency of MRI review, ophthalmology, and neurosurgical escalation. Source: PITUITARY_PROLACTINOMA_2023; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Inspect for galactorrhea: Inspect for spontaneous discharge and, only when clinically appropriate, gently express from the areola toward the nipple while preserving privacy and consent. Findings: Absent / Spontaneous discharge / Expressible discharge / Bloody/unilateral discharge / Unable/deferred. Target: gonadal axis, prolactin, androgen excess/deficiency, or reproductive endocrine phenotype Management: Galactorrhea changes prolactin interpretation and pituitary workup priority. Diagnostic workup and reference values:
- Serum prolactin; repeat/macroprolactin if mild/discordant.: Interpret with local lab ranges. Reference anchors: Prolactin upper limit often about 20 ng/mL in men and 25 ng/mL in women, but lab, pregnancy, lactation, and macroprolactin matter. Male total testosterone should be early morning and repeated; lower limit often around 264-300 ng/dL depending assay. IGF-1, LH/FSH, estradiol, AMH, and pediatric growth labs require age/sex/puberty-specific ranges. Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects. Rationale: Confirms the diagnosis, identifies mimics or complications, or establishes a baseline that changes treatment for Prolactinoma (Benign pituitary tumor). Source: PITUITARY_PROLACTINOMA_2023.

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- Prolactin upper limit often about 20 ng/mL in men and 25 ng/mL in women, but lab, pregnancy, lactation, and macroprolactin matter.
- Male total testosterone should be early morning and repeated; lower limit often around 264-300 ng/dL depending assay.
- IGF-1, LH/FSH, estradiol, AMH, and pediatric growth labs require age/sex/puberty-specific ranges.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Visual field deficit, severe headache/apoplexy, cranial nerve palsy, pregnancy with macroadenoma symptoms.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Prolactinoma (Benign pituitary tumor) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: PITUITARY_PROLACTINOMA_2023.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Prolactinoma (Benign pituitary tumor) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: PITUITARY_PROLACTINOMA_2023.
- Pituitary apoplexy, acute severe headache, visual field deficit, cranial nerve palsy, adrenal crisis, severe hypernatremia, inability to drink, or macroadenoma symptoms in pregnancy.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Prolactinoma (Benign pituitary tumor) presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: PITUITARY_PROLACTINOMA_2023.

Results that change management:
- Mass effect or macroadenoma changes urgency and ophthalmology/neurosurgery involvement. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Prolactinoma (Benign pituitary tumor). Source: PITUITARY_PROLACTINOMA_2023.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Prolactinoma (Benign pituitary tumor). Source: ES_HYPERPROLACTINEMIA_2011.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Prolactinoma (Benign pituitary tumor). Source: PITUITARY_PROLACTINOMA_2023.
- Central adrenal insufficiency must be addressed before thyroid hormone escalation; pituitary mass effect changes ophthalmology/neurosurgery urgency. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Prolactinoma (Benign pituitary tumor). Source: ES_HYPERPROLACTINEMIA_2011.
- Confirmed hormone excess/deficiency plus MRI finding changes endocrine, neurosurgical, fertility, and replacement-therapy pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Prolactinoma (Benign pituitary tumor). Source: PITUITARY_PROLACTINOMA_2023.

## 33. Acromegaly

Category: Pituitary Gland Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module acromegaly_v1; validated intent matches: acromegaly_intent_v1 (279)
Guidelines: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014; PITUITARY_ACROMEGALY_2021; ACROMEGALY_DIAGNOSIS_REMISSION_2024; ACROMEGALY_COMPLICATIONS_2026

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Acromegaly. Source: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Acromegaly. Source: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014.

Clinical questions:
- Any sweating, enlarged hands/feet, ring or shoe-size change, jaw/facial change, joint pain, sleep apnea, headaches, diabetes, hypertension, or colon-polyp history suggesting acromegaly complications? Options: No / Sweating / Enlarged hands/feet / Ring / Shoe-size change / Jaw/facial change / Joint pain / Sleep apnea / Headaches / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Acromegaly needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes growth-hormone excess probability, IGF-1 interpretation, pituitary imaging priority, and screening for sleep apnea, cardiometabolic, joint, and colon-polyp complications. Source: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014.
- Any loud snoring, witnessed apneas, morning headaches, daytime sleepiness, resistant hypertension, or CPAP use? Options: No / Loud snoring / Witnessed apneas / Morning headaches / Daytime sleepiness / Resistant hypertension / CPAP / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Acromegaly needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes growth-hormone excess probability, IGF-1 interpretation, pituitary imaging priority, and screening for sleep apnea, cardiometabolic, joint, and colon-polyp complications. Source: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014.
- Any new, worsening, resistant, or treatment-limiting hypertension or diabetes that changes endocrine severity, complication screening, or medication choice? Options: No / New / Worsening / Resistant / Treatment-limiting hypertension / Diabetes that changes endocrine severity / Complication screening / Medication choice / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Acromegaly therapy unsafe. Management: The answer changes growth-hormone excess probability, IGF-1 interpretation, pituitary imaging priority, and screening for sleep apnea, cardiometabolic, joint, and colon-polyp complications. Source: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014.
- Any eye pain, redness, light sensitivity, bulging eyes, double vision, reduced vision, or trouble closing the eyelids? Options: No / Eye pain / Redness / Light sensitivity / Bulging eyes / Double vision / Reduced vision / Trouble closing the eyelids / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Acromegaly needs urgent evaluation today. Management: A positive answer changes pituitary mass-effect urgency, MRI/visual-field review, pituitary hormone testing, and neurosurgical or ophthalmology escalation for Acromegaly. Source: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014.
- Any spontaneous or expressible nipple discharge, breast tenderness, headaches, visual symptoms, or medications that raise prolactin? Options: No / Spontaneous / Expressible nipple discharge / Breast tenderness / Headaches / Visual symptoms / Medications that raise prolactin / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Acromegaly therapy unsafe. Management: A positive answer changes pituitary mass-effect urgency, MRI/visual-field review, pituitary hormone testing, and neurosurgical or ophthalmology escalation for Acromegaly. Source: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014.
- When was the last menstrual period, how regular are cycles, and has bleeding changed from baseline? Options: Not possible / Possible / Known pregnant/postpartum / Timing/dating known / Unknown / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Acromegaly needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes pituitary-gonadal axis testing, hypopituitarism assessment, fertility counseling, and pituitary treatment timing for Acromegaly. Source: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014.

- None.

Rationale: Identifies dangerous Acromegaly presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014.

Results that change management:
- Elevated IGF-1 plus inadequate GH suppression changes to pituitary MRI/surgical pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Acromegaly. Source: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Acromegaly. Source: PITUITARY_ACROMEGALY_2021.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Acromegaly. Source: ACROMEGALY_DIAGNOSIS_REMISSION_2024.
- Central adrenal insufficiency must be addressed before thyroid hormone escalation; pituitary mass effect changes ophthalmology/neurosurgery urgency. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Acromegaly. Source: ACROMEGALY_COMPLICATIONS_2026.
- Confirmed hormone excess/deficiency plus MRI finding changes endocrine, neurosurgical, fertility, and replacement-therapy pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Acromegaly. Source: ES_ACROMEGALY_2014.

TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context. Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay. Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- 8 AM cortisol <3 ug/dL strongly suggests adrenal insufficiency; >15-18 ug/dL often makes it unlikely, context dependent.
- Cosyntropin peak cortisol <18 ug/dL is a traditional abnormal cutoff; modern assays may use about 14-15 ug/dL.
- Sodium about 135-145 mmol/L; potassium about 3.5-5.0 mmol/L.
- TSH typical adult range about 0.4-4.0 mIU/L; use local lab, pregnancy, and illness context.
- Free T4 typical adult range about 0.8-1.8 ng/dL; use local assay.
- T3, TRAb/TSI, TPO Ab, and thyroglobulin Ab are assay-specific.
- Prolactin upper limit often about 20 ng/mL in men and 25 ng/mL in women, but lab, pregnancy, lactation, and macroprolactin matter.
- Male total testosterone should be early morning and repeated; lower limit often around 264-300 ng/dL depending assay.
- IGF-1, LH/FSH, estradiol, AMH, and pediatric growth labs require age/sex/puberty-specific ranges.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Adrenal crisis, pituitary apoplexy, visual loss, severe hyponatremia.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypopituitarism presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_HYPOPITUITARISM_2016.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypopituitarism presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_HYPOPITUITARISM_2016.
- Pituitary apoplexy, acute severe headache, visual field deficit, cranial nerve palsy, adrenal crisis, severe hypernatremia, inability to drink, or macroadenoma symptoms in pregnancy.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Hypopituitarism presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ES_HYPOPITUITARISM_2016.

Results that change management:
- Central adrenal insufficiency must be addressed before thyroid hormone escalation. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypopituitarism. Source: ES_HYPOPITUITARISM_2016.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypopituitarism. Source: ES_HYPOPITUITARISM_2016.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypopituitarism. Source: ES_HYPOPITUITARISM_2016.
- Central adrenal insufficiency must be addressed before thyroid hormone escalation; pituitary mass effect changes ophthalmology/neurosurgery urgency. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypopituitarism. Source: ES_HYPOPITUITARISM_2016.
- Confirmed hormone excess/deficiency plus MRI finding changes endocrine, neurosurgical, fertility, and replacement-therapy pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Hypopituitarism. Source: ES_HYPOPITUITARISM_2016.

## 36. Diabetes Insipidus

Category: Pituitary Gland Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module diabetes_insipidus_v1; validated intent matches: diabetes_insipidus_intent_v1 (322)
Guidelines: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026; SFE_CDI_2018

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- Measure orthostatic blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Orthostasis changes hypernatremia risk and need for monitored fluids. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- Document mental status: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Confusion or somnolence changes hypernatremia severity, disposition, and monitored correction strategy. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.

Clinical questions:
- What is the approximate 24-hour urine volume, and has urine output changed from baseline? Options: 24-hour urine volume / Urine output changed from baseline / Other ___. Purpose: Defines the patient-specific context needed to interpret endocrine tests, avoid common mimics, and choose the safest next step for Diabetes Insipidus. Management: The pattern changes fluid-sodium interpretation, urine testing priority, desmopressin or hydration safety, and monitoring needs for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- How many times do you urinate overnight, and is this new or worsening? Options: Nocturia frequency / New or worsening / Worsening / Other ___. Purpose: Defines the patient-specific context needed to interpret endocrine tests, avoid common mimics, and choose the safest next step for Diabetes Insipidus. Management: The answer changes the leading Diabetes Insipidus pathway by refining severity, mimics, confirmatory testing, treatment safety, and follow-up timing. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.

Options: Fluid intake / Urine output / Polyuria / Polydipsia / Overnight urination / Thirst intensity / Access to water / Dehydration / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Diabetes Insipidus needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes medication-induced polyuria assessment, sodium monitoring, urine-osmolality interpretation, desmopressin safety, and hydration planning for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- Do you have reliable access to water, and are thirst, intake, or mental status limiting safe hydration? Options: Reliable water access / Thirst/intake limits hydration / Intake / Mental status limiting safe hydration / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Diabetes Insipidus needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes medication-induced polyuria assessment, sodium monitoring, urine-osmolality interpretation, desmopressin safety, and hydration planning for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- Any lithium, demeclocycline, amphotericin, diuretic, SGLT2 inhibitor, glucocorticoid, desmopressin, fluid restriction, or recent medication change affecting polyuria, sodium, thirst, or kidney concentrating ability? Options: No / Lithium / Demeclocycline / Amphotericin / Diuretic / SGLT2 inhibitor / Glucocorticoid / Desmopressin / Fluid restriction / Other ___. Purpose: Identifies exposures, physiologic states, or treatment changes that can explain abnormal results or make Diabetes Insipidus therapy unsafe. Management: The answer changes medication-induced polyuria assessment, sodium monitoring, urine-osmolality interpretation, desmopressin safety, and hydration planning for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- Any kidney stones, constipation, polyuria, polydipsia, bone pain, confusion, dehydration, or reduced kidney function? Options: No / Kidney stones / Constipation / Polyuria / Polydipsia / Bone pain / Confusion / Dehydration / Reduced kidney function / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Diabetes Insipidus needs urgent evaluation today. Management: The answer changes medication-induced polyuria assessment, sodium monitoring, urine-osmolality interpretation, desmopressin safety, and hydration planning for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- Any new headache, peripheral vision loss, double vision, eye movement pain, sudden severe headache, nausea, or pituitary surgery/radiation history? Options: No / New headache / Peripheral vision loss / Double vision / Eye movement pain / Sudden severe headache / Nausea / Pituitary surgery/radiation history / Other ___. Purpose: Defines symptom severity, tempo, complications, and whether Diabetes Insipidus needs urgent evaluation today. Management: A positive answer changes pituitary mass-effect urgency, MRI/visual-field review, pituitary hormone testing, and neurosurgical or ophthalmology escalation for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.

Conditional history add-ons:
- None.

Core physical exam maneuvers:
- Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid and desmopressin monitoring urgency. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Test capillary refill: Apply brief pressure to a fingertip or toe and record return of color while considering temperature, perfusion, and vascular disease. Findings: Brisk / Delayed / Mottled/cool / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Delayed refill changes dehydration severity, fluid urgency, and monitored-care threshold. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Test skin turgor: Gently pinch skin over a clinically appropriate site and observe recoil, interpreting cautiously in older adults or chronic skin changes. Findings: Normal recoil / Reduced recoil / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Reduced turgor supports clinically important dehydration but must be interpreted cautiously with age and skin changes. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Test confrontation visual fields: Test each eye separately by confrontation, comparing peripheral fields with the examiner's field while the patient fixes on a central target. Findings: Full / Bitemporal deficit / Other field deficit / Unable to assess. Target: pituitary/sellar mass effect or cranial nerve involvement Management: Field loss changes emergency imaging and neurosurgical urgency. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Test extraocular movements: Ask the patient to follow a target through cardinal gaze positions and observe for limitation, pain, diplopia, or nystagmus. Findings: Full / Restricted / Diplopia / Painful / Unable to assess. Target: pituitary/sellar mass effect, cavernous sinus involvement, or cranial nerve III/IV/VI dysfunction Management: Ophthalmoplegia changes emergency evaluation and neurosurgical urgency. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none

Reference ranges / diagnostic thresholds:
- Serum sodium normal about 135-145 mmol/L; SFE inpatient CDI guidance: 146-149 mild, 150-159 moderate, >160 severe hypernatremia.
- Urine osmolality <300 mOsm/kg is hypotonic; >800 often argues against DI.
- Use local laboratory intervals and assay-specific cutoffs; endocrine immunoassays are affected by pregnancy, age, sex, acute illness, binding proteins, biotin, and medication effects.

Red flags:
- Hypernatremia, inability to drink, impaired consciousness, postoperative pituitary patient without desmopressin access.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Diabetes Insipidus presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- Hemodynamic instability, altered mental status, severe electrolyte/glucose abnormality, arrhythmia, airway compromise, or vision threat requires urgent escalation.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Diabetes Insipidus presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- Pituitary apoplexy, acute severe headache, visual field deficit, cranial nerve palsy, adrenal crisis, severe hypernatremia, inability to drink, or macroadenoma symptoms in pregnancy.: Escalate urgently, reassess severity, and evaluate for dangerous mimics or complications. Rationale: Identifies dangerous Diabetes Insipidus presentations that should override routine outpatient workup and prompt urgent escalation. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.

Results that change management:
- Hypernatremia or impaired water access changes to urgent monitored fluid/desmopressin pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- Unstable physiology, endocrine crisis, pregnancy-critical medication issue, or dangerous electrolyte/glucose abnormality changes disposition to urgent monitored care. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: SFE_CDI_2018.
- Discordant or borderline endocrine tests should be confirmed and interpreted with timing, assay, medication, pregnancy, and acute illness context before irreversible treatment. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.
- Central adrenal insufficiency must be addressed before thyroid hormone escalation; pituitary mass effect changes ophthalmology/neurosurgery urgency. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: SFE_CDI_2018.
- Confirmed hormone excess/deficiency plus MRI finding changes endocrine, neurosurgical, fertility, and replacement-therapy pathway. Rationale: Links a result or bedside finding to a concrete management change for Diabetes Insipidus. Source: ENDOTEXT_DI_2026.

## 37. Cushing's Disease (Pituitary-dependent Cushing's)

Category: Pituitary Gland Disorders
Quality status: pass
Current app support: installed module cushings_disease_v1; validated intent matches: cushings_disease_intent_v1 (420)
Guidelines: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008; ES_CUSHING_TREATMENT_2015; ES_HYPOPITUITARISM_2016

Basic bedside data / safety checks:
- Measure blood pressure: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Hypotension or severe hypertension changes acuity, medication safety, fluid strategy, and escalation. Rationale: Targets hemodynamic safety, hypertension or hypotension severity, and medication or fluid-safety context; positive, negative, or unable-to-assess findings guide escalation, diagnostic testing, treatment safety, or specialty planning for Cushing's Disease (Pituitary-dependent Cushing's). Source: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008.
- Measure heart rate: Check and document as baseline bedside data for this workup. Tachycardia, bradycardia, or irregular rhythm changes acuity, ECG need, and treatment urgency. Rationale: Screens severity and immediate safety findings that can change triage, monitoring, fluids, or urgent escalation for Cushing's Disease (Pituitary-dependent Cushing's). Source: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008.

Conditional exam add-ons:
- Test confrontation visual fields: Test each eye separately by confrontation, comparing peripheral fields with the examiner's field while the patient fixes on a central target. Findings: Full / Bitemporal deficit / Other field deficit / Unable to assess. Target: pituitary/sellar mass effect or cranial nerve involvement Management: Field loss changes emergency imaging and neurosurgical urgency. Source: ES_CUSHING_DX_2008; LR+ n/a; LR- n/a; difficulty easy; 1 min; equipment none
- Test extraocular movements: Ask the patient to follow a target through cardinal gaze positions and observe for limitation, pain, diplopia, or nystagmus. Findings: Full / Restricted / Diplopia / Painful / Unable to assess. Target: pituitary/sellar mass effect, cavernous sinus involvement, or cranial nerve III/IV/VI dysfunction Management: Ophthalmoplegia changes emergency evaluation and neurosurgical urgency. - Inspect mucous membranes for dehydration: Inspect oral mucosa and tongue moisture with attention to dry mucosa, cracked lips, and overall hydration context. Findings: Moist / Dry / Very dry / Unable to assess. Target: volume status, dehydration severity, or peripheral perfusion Management: Dehydration changes fluid strategy, lab urgency, and monitoring needs.
